User: I first need to check the input data in ../dlc_long.csv as we saw that there may be identity flips between the two mice. ../dlc_long.csv contains the image coordinates of mouse0 and mouse1 body parts for all video frames. Please write a stand alone .py program that reads --dlc and --topIn --frontIn and --sideIn videos (I can give the dlc generated video files), superimpose the body parts in the same style as in the previous programs to the videos and write them to --topOut --frontOut --sideOut

Assistant: from pathlib import Path
import os, stat, textwrap

script = r"""#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
script += r'''
"""
overlay_dlc_on_videos.py

Reads a DeepLabCut-style long-format CSV (dlc_long.csv) with columns:
  frame, camera, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood

Overlays body-part detections (and optional skeleton edges) onto three input videos
(top/front/side) and writes three annotated output videos.

Example:
  python overlay_dlc_on_videos.py \
    --dlc ../dlc_long.csv \
    --topIn top.mp4 --frontIn front.mp4 --sideIn side.mp4 \
    --topOut top_anno.mp4 --frontOut front_anno.mp4 --sideOut side_anno.mp4 \
    --template ../mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
    --likelihood-min 0.2 --draw-labels

Notes:
- Requires opencv-python (cv2). In your conda env: conda install -c conda-forge opencv
- If --template is provided, the script parses [EDGES] and draws a skeleton.
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd

import cv2


# -----------------------------
# Template edges (optional)
# -----------------------------
def parse_edges_from_template(path: str | Path) -> List[Tuple[str, str]]:
    """Parse [EDGES] section with lines: 'nodeA nodeB'."""
    p = Path(path)
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]] = []
    in_edges = False
    for line in p.read_text(encoding="utf-8").splitlines():
        s = line.strip()
        if not s:
            continue
        if s.upper() == "[EDGES]":
            in_edges = True
            continue
        if s.startswith("[") and s.endswith("]") and s.upper() != "[EDGES]":
            in_edges = False
        if in_edges:
            parts = s.split()
            if len(parts) == 2:
                edges.append((parts[0], parts[1]))
    return edges


# -----------------------------
# Drawing helpers
# -----------------------------
def make_color_map(individuals: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Tuple[int, int, int]]:
    """
    Deterministic BGR colors (OpenCV).
    First two: white and green (like previous scripts).
    """
    colors = [
        (255, 255, 255),  # white
        (80, 220, 80),    # green-ish
        (220, 80, 80),    # blue-ish/red-ish (BGR)
        (80, 80, 220),
        (220, 220, 80),
        (220, 80, 220),
    ]
    cmap: Dict[str, Tuple[int, int, int]] = {}
    for i, ind in enumerate(individuals):
        cmap[ind] = colors[i % len(colors)]
    return cmap


def overlay_frame(
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    rows: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    rows contains detections for a single (camera, frame).
    Draws:
      - skeleton edges (if edges != None)
      - nodes as circles
      - optional labels
    """
    if rows.empty:
        return frame_bgr

    # individuals present in this frame (sorted for stable color assignment)
    inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
    cmap = make_color_map(inds)

    # Build lookup: (ind, bodypart) -> (x,y,lik)
    coords: Dict[Tuple[str, str], Tuple[float, float, float]] = {}
    for r in rows.itertuples(index=False):
        ind = str(r.individual)
        bp = str(r.bodypart)
        x = float(r.x) if pd.notna(r.x) else np.nan
        y = float(r.y) if pd.notna(r.y) else np.nan
        lik = float(r.likelihood) if pd.notna(r.likelihood) else 0.0
        coords[(ind, bp)] = (x, y, lik)

    # Draw skeleton edges first
    if edges:
        for ind in inds:
            col = cmap[ind]
            for a, b in edges:
                ka = (ind, a)
                kb = (ind, b)
                if ka not in coords or kb not in coords:
                    continue
                xa, ya, la = coords[ka]
                xb, yb, lb = coords[kb]
                if la < likelihood_min or lb < likelihood_min:
                    continue
                if not (np.isfinite(xa) and np.isfinite(ya) and np.isfinite(xb) and np.isfinite(yb)):
                    continue
                cv2.line(frame_bgr, (int(xa), int(ya)), (int(xb), int(yb)), col, 2, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # Draw nodes
    for ind in inds:
        col = cmap[ind]
        for (i_ind, bp), (x, y, lik) in coords.items():
            if i_ind != ind:
                continue
            if lik < likelihood_min:
                continue
            if not (np.isfinite(x) and np.isfinite(y)):
                continue
            cv2.circle(frame_bgr, (int(x), int(y)), 4, col, -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
            if draw_labels:
                txt = f"{ind}:{bp}"
                cv2.putText(
                    frame_bgr,
                    txt,
                    (int(x) + 6, int(y) - 6),
                    cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX,
                    float(label_scale),
                    col,
                    int(label_thickness),
                    cv2.LINE_AA,
                )
    return frame_bgr


# -----------------------------
# Video processing
# -----------------------------
def overlay_video(
    in_path: str | Path,
    out_path: str | Path,
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    in_path = str(in_path)
    out_path = str(out_path)

    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(in_path)
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open input video: {in_path}")

    w = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(out_path, fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open output video for writing: {out_path}")

    # Sort for efficient per-frame scan
    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)
    idx = 0

    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        # Advance idx to current frame
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1

        if idx > start:
            rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx]
        else:
            rows = df_cam.iloc[0:0]  # empty

        out_frame = overlay_frame(
            frame,
            rows,
            edges=edges,
            likelihood_min=likelihood_min,
            draw_labels=draw_labels,
            label_scale=label_scale,
            label_thickness=label_thickness,
        )
        writer.write(out_frame)
        frame_idx += 1

    cap.release()
    writer.release()


# -----------------------------
# CLI
# -----------------------------
def build_arg_parser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(prog="overlay_dlc_on_videos.py")
    p.add_argument("--dlc", required=True, help="Path to dlc_long.csv")

    p.add_argument("--topIn", required=True, help="Input top camera video")
    p.add_argument("--frontIn", required=True, help="Input front camera video")
    p.add_argument("--sideIn", required=True, help="Input side camera video")

    p.add_argument("--topOut", required=True, help="Output annotated top video")
    p.add_argument("--frontOut", required=True, help="Output annotated front video")
    p.add_argument("--sideOut", required=True, help="Output annotated side video")

    p.add_argument("--topCam", default="cam1_top", help="Camera name in CSV for top view (default cam1_top)")
    p.add_argument("--frontCam", default="cam2_front", help="Camera name in CSV for front view (default cam2_front)")
    p.add_argument("--sideCam", default="cam3_side", help="Camera name in CSV for side view (default cam3_side)")

    p.add_argument("--template", default=None, help="Optional template file to draw skeleton edges ([EDGES] section)")

    p.add_argument("--likelihood-min", type=float, default=0.2, help="Only draw points with likelihood >= this (default 0.2)")

    p.add_argument("--draw-labels", action="store_true", help="Draw text labels 'mouse:bodypart' near each point")
    p.add_argument("--label-scale", type=float, default=0.4, help="OpenCV font scale for labels (default 0.4)")
    p.add_argument("--label-thickness", type=int, default=1, help="Label thickness (default 1)")

    p.add_argument("--force-fps", type=float, default=None, help="Override output FPS (else use input video FPS)")

    return p


def main() -> int:
    args = build_arg_parser().parse_args()

    dlc_path = Path(args.dlc)
    if not dlc_path.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(dlc_path)

    df = pd.read_csv(dlc_path)
    required = {"frame", "camera", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"}
    missing = required - set(df.columns)
    if missing:
        raise ValueError(f"dlc CSV missing columns: {sorted(missing)}")

    edges = None
    if args.template:
        edges = parse_edges_from_template(args.template)
        if not edges:
            print("[warn] Template provided but no edges were found; drawing only points.")

    # Filter and process each camera separately
    def df_for_cam(cam_name: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
        return df[df["camera"].astype(str) == str(cam_name)][["frame", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"]].copy()

    print("Loading DLC rows...")
    df_top = df_for_cam(args.topCam)
    df_front = df_for_cam(args.frontCam)
    df_side = df_for_cam(args.sideCam)
    print(f"Rows per view: top={len(df_top)}, front={len(df_front)}, side={len(df_side)}")

    print("Annotating top video...")
    overlay_video(args.topIn, args.topOut, df_top, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.topOut}")

    print("Annotating front video...")
    overlay_video(args.frontIn, args.frontOut, df_front, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.frontOut}")

    print("Annotating side video...")
    overlay_video(args.sideIn, args.sideOut, df_side, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.sideOut}")

    return 0


if __name__ == "__main__":
    raise SystemExit(main())
'''

out = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos.py")
out.write_text(script, encoding="utf-8")
os.chmod(out, os.stat(out).st_mode | stat.S_IEXEC)
str(out)

Assistant: Here you go — a **stand-alone** Python program that:

- reads `--dlc` (your `dlc_long.csv`)
- reads three input videos `--topIn --frontIn --sideIn`
- overlays the DLC detections in the **same visual style** we’ve been using (circles + optional skeleton edges)
- writes three output videos `--topOut --frontOut --sideOut`

[Download overlay_dlc_on_videos.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos.py)

## Usage

```bash
python overlay_dlc_on_videos.py \
  --dlc ../dlc_long.csv \
  --topIn top.mp4 --frontIn front.mp4 --sideIn side.mp4 \
  --topOut top_anno.mp4 --frontOut front_anno.mp4 --sideOut side_anno.mp4 \
  --template ../mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
  --likelihood-min 0.2
```

### Notes / options
- `--template` is optional. If provided, the script parses the `[EDGES]` section and draws the skeleton. If omitted, it draws only points.
- `--likelihood-min` controls what gets drawn (default 0.2). For identity-flip debugging, you may want `0.1–0.3`.
- `--draw-labels` adds `mouse:bodypart` text next to each point (useful for spotting flips):
  ```bash
  --draw-labels
  ```

- If your camera names in the CSV differ, override:
  ```bash
  --topCam cam1_top --frontCam cam2_front --sideCam cam3_side
  ```

- Output FPS defaults to the input video FPS. If needed:
  ```bash
  --force-fps 10
  ```

---

## What you’ll get
- `top_anno.mp4`: top view with overlaid detections
- `front_anno.mp4`: front view with overlaid detections
- `side_anno.mp4`: side view with overlaid detections

This should make identity flips obvious (especially with `--draw-labels`).

User: It is very exciting, as there are not only identity switches between the two mice, but also body parts occasionally flip to the wrong mouse. That is something we do not need in the bundle adjustment that is only a method that expects good approximations and applies a linearized least-squares strategy at the approximations.

Anyways, we will investigate these problems later. For now please (only) extend the program by adding a parameter --joinedVideo that is of the same size/resolution as the other videos but contains the side video in the bottom left quarter (resample professionally to avoid aliasing effects), the front video in the bottom right quarter and the top video in the top right quarter. (Leave the top left quarter empty.)

src = src_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")

# We'll create a v2 file with joined video support.
v2 = src

# Insert new function overlay_three_and_join before CLI section. We'll find marker "# -----------------------------\n# CLI"
marker = "# -----------------------------\n# CLI"
insert_pos = v2.find(marker)
assert insert_pos != -1

join_func = r"""

def overlay_three_and_join(
    top_in: str | Path, front_in: str | Path, side_in: str | Path,
    joined_out: str | Path,
    df_top: pd.DataFrame, df_front: pd.DataFrame, df_side: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    """
    Reads the three videos synchronously, overlays detections, and writes a joined video
    of the SAME resolution as the inputs:

      +-------------------+-------------------+
      | (empty)           | top (resized)     |
      +-------------------+-------------------+
      | side (resized)    | front (resized)   |
      +-------------------+-------------------+

    Each sub-view is downsampled to quarter size using INTER_AREA to minimize aliasing.
    """
    top_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(top_in))
    front_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(front_in))
    side_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(side_in))
    if not top_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open top input video: {top_in}")
    if not front_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open front input video: {front_in}")
    if not side_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open side input video: {side_in}")

    w = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))

    # Use top video FPS as reference unless overridden
    fps_in = float(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    # Ensure other videos are same size; if not, we'll resize them before placing.
    w2 = int(front_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h2 = int(front_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    w3 = int(side_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h3 = int(side_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(joined_out), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open joined output video for writing: {joined_out}")

    # Pre-sort CSV subsets for fast frame slicing
    def prep(df_cam: pd.DataFrame) -> Tuple[pd.DataFrame, np.ndarray]:
        df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
        return df_cam, df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)

    df_top, fr_top = prep(df_top)
    df_front, fr_front = prep(df_front)
    df_side, fr_side = prep(df_side)

    idx_top = idx_front = idx_side = 0
    n_top, n_front, n_side = len(df_top), len(df_front), len(df_side)

    def slice_rows(df_cam: pd.DataFrame, fr_arr: np.ndarray, idx: int, n: int, frame_idx: int):
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]
        return rows, idx

    half_w = w // 2
    half_h = h // 2

    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok_t, frame_t = top_cap.read()
        ok_f, frame_f = front_cap.read()
        ok_s, frame_s = side_cap.read()
        if not (ok_t and ok_f and ok_s):
            break

        # Normalize sizes to top frame size if needed
        if frame_f.shape[1] != w or frame_f.shape[0] != h:
            frame_f = cv2.resize(frame_f, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
        if frame_s.shape[1] != w or frame_s.shape[0] != h:
            frame_s = cv2.resize(frame_s, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)

        rows_t, idx_top = slice_rows(df_top, fr_top, idx_top, n_top, frame_idx)
        rows_f, idx_front = slice_rows(df_front, fr_front, idx_front, n_front, frame_idx)
        rows_s, idx_side = slice_rows(df_side, fr_side, idx_side, n_side, frame_idx)

        frame_t_anno = overlay_frame(frame_t, rows_t, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_f_anno = overlay_frame(frame_f, rows_f, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_s_anno = overlay_frame(frame_s, rows_s, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)

        # Downsample to quarter-size using INTER_AREA (best for downsampling)
        top_small = cv2.resize(frame_t_anno, (half_w, half_h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        front_small = cv2.resize(frame_f_anno, (half_w, half_h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        side_small = cv2.resize(frame_s_anno, (half_w, half_h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)

        canvas = np.zeros((h, w, 3), dtype=np.uint8)

        # Place: top in top-right
        canvas[0:half_h, half_w:w] = top_small
        # side in bottom-left
        canvas[half_h:h, 0:half_w] = side_small
        # front in bottom-right
        canvas[half_h:h, half_w:w] = front_small

        writer.write(canvas)
        frame_idx += 1

    top_cap.release()
    front_cap.release()
    side_cap.release()
    writer.release()
"""

v2 = v2[:insert_pos] + join_func + v2[insert_pos:]

    if args.joinedVideo:
        print("Writing joined mosaic video...")
        overlay_three_and_join(
            args.topIn, args.frontIn, args.sideIn,
            args.joinedVideo,
            df_top, df_front, df_side,
            edges=edges,
            likelihood_min=args.likelihood_min,
            draw_labels=args.draw_labels,
            label_scale=args.label_scale,
            label_thickness=args.label_thickness,
            force_fps=args.force_fps,
        )
        print(f"Wrote: {args.joinedVideo}")
"""
# Insert just before "return 0"
v2 = v2.replace("    print(f\"Wrote: {args.sideOut}\")\n\n    return 0\n",
                "    print(f\"Wrote: {args.sideOut}\")\n\n" + main_insertion + "\n    return 0\n")

Assistant: from pathlib import Path
import os, stat

code = """#!/usr/bin/env python3
\"\"\"
overlay_dlc_on_videos_v2.py

Reads a DeepLabCut-style long-format CSV (dlc_long.csv) with columns:
  frame, camera, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood
(Extra columns like scorer are ignored.)

Overlays body-part detections (and optional skeleton edges from a template [EDGES] section)
onto three input videos (top/front/side) and writes three annotated output videos.

Additionally, if --joinedVideo is provided, writes a single mosaic video of the SAME
resolution as the input videos:

  +-------------------+-------------------+
  | (empty)           | top (downsampled) |
  +-------------------+-------------------+
  | side (downsampled)| front (downsampled)|
  +-------------------+-------------------+

Downsampling uses cv2.INTER_AREA to reduce aliasing.

Requires: opencv (cv2), numpy, pandas
\"\"\"

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import cv2


# -----------------------------
# Template edges (optional)
# -----------------------------
def parse_edges_from_template(path: str | Path) -> List[Tuple[str, str]]:
    \"\"\"Parse [EDGES] section with lines: 'nodeA nodeB'.\"\"\"
    p = Path(path)
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]] = []
    in_edges = False
    for line in p.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\").splitlines():
        s = line.strip()
        if not s:
            continue
        if s.upper() == \"[EDGES]\":
            in_edges = True
            continue
        if s.startswith(\"[\") and s.endswith(\"]\") and s.upper() != \"[EDGES]\":
            in_edges = False
        if in_edges:
            parts = s.split()
            if len(parts) == 2:
                edges.append((parts[0], parts[1]))
    return edges


# -----------------------------
# Drawing helpers
# -----------------------------
def make_color_map(individuals: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Tuple[int, int, int]]:
    \"\"\"Deterministic BGR colors (OpenCV).\"\"\"
    colors = [
        (255, 255, 255),  # white
        (80, 220, 80),    # green-ish
        (220, 80, 80),
        (80, 80, 220),
        (220, 220, 80),
        (220, 80, 220),
    ]
    return {ind: colors[i % len(colors)] for i, ind in enumerate(individuals)}


def overlay_frame(
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    rows: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
) -> np.ndarray:
    \"\"\"Overlay detections for a single frame (already filtered to one camera).\"\"\"
    if rows.empty:
        return frame_bgr

    inds = sorted(rows[\"individual\"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
    cmap = make_color_map(inds)

    coords: Dict[Tuple[str, str], Tuple[float, float, float]] = {}
    for r in rows.itertuples(index=False):
        ind = str(r.individual)
        bp = str(r.bodypart)
        x = float(r.x) if pd.notna(r.x) else np.nan
        y = float(r.y) if pd.notna(r.y) else np.nan
        lik = float(r.likelihood) if pd.notna(r.likelihood) else 0.0
        coords[(ind, bp)] = (x, y, lik)

    # skeleton
    if edges:
        for ind in inds:
            col = cmap[ind]
            for a, b in edges:
                ka, kb = (ind, a), (ind, b)
                if ka not in coords or kb not in coords:
                    continue
                xa, ya, la = coords[ka]
                xb, yb, lb = coords[kb]
                if la < likelihood_min or lb < likelihood_min:
                    continue
                if not (np.isfinite(xa) and np.isfinite(ya) and np.isfinite(xb) and np.isfinite(yb)):
                    continue
                cv2.line(frame_bgr, (int(xa), int(ya)), (int(xb), int(yb)), col, 2, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # points
    for ind in inds:
        col = cmap[ind]
        for (i_ind, bp), (x, y, lik) in coords.items():
            if i_ind != ind:
                continue
            if lik < likelihood_min:
                continue
            if not (np.isfinite(x) and np.isfinite(y)):
                continue
            cv2.circle(frame_bgr, (int(x), int(y)), 4, col, -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
            if draw_labels:
                cv2.putText(
                    frame_bgr,
                    f\"{ind}:{bp}\",
                    (int(x) + 6, int(y) - 6),
                    cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX,
                    float(label_scale),
                    col,
                    int(label_thickness),
                    cv2.LINE_AA,
                )
    return frame_bgr


# -----------------------------
# Per-video overlay
# -----------------------------
def overlay_video(
    in_path: str | Path,
    out_path: str | Path,
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> Tuple[int, int, float, int]:
    \"\"\"Overlay detections onto a single video. Returns (w,h,fps,num_frames_written).\"\"\"
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(in_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open input video: {in_path}\")

    w = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*\"mp4v\")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(out_path), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open output video: {out_path}\")

    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values(\"frame\").reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam[\"frame\"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)
    idx = 0

    frame_idx = 0
    written = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1

        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]
        out_frame = overlay_frame(frame, rows, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        writer.write(out_frame)
        frame_idx += 1
        written += 1

    cap.release()
    writer.release()
    return w, h, fps, written


# -----------------------------
# Joined mosaic writer
# -----------------------------
def overlay_three_and_join(
    top_in: str | Path, front_in: str | Path, side_in: str | Path,
    joined_out: str | Path,
    df_top: pd.DataFrame, df_front: pd.DataFrame, df_side: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    top_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(top_in))
    front_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(front_in))
    side_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(side_in))
    if not top_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open top input video: {top_in}\")
    if not front_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open front input video: {front_in}\")
    if not side_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open side input video: {side_in}\")

    w = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    # quadrant sizes (handle odd sizes by assigning remainder to right/bottom)
    w_left = w // 2
    w_right = w - w_left
    h_top = h // 2
    h_bottom = h - h_top

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*\"mp4v\")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(joined_out), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f\"Could not open joined output video: {joined_out}\")

    def prep(df_cam: pd.DataFrame):
        df_cam = df_cam.sort_values(\"frame\").reset_index(drop=True)
        return df_cam, df_cam[\"frame\"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)

    df_top, fr_top = prep(df_top)
    df_front, fr_front = prep(df_front)
    df_side, fr_side = prep(df_side)
    idx_top = idx_front = idx_side = 0

    def slice_rows(df_cam, fr_arr, idx, frame_idx):
        n = len(fr_arr)
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]
        return rows, idx

    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok_t, frame_t = top_cap.read()
        ok_f, frame_f = front_cap.read()
        ok_s, frame_s = side_cap.read()
        if not (ok_t and ok_f and ok_s):
            break

        # If other videos differ in size, resize to top size BEFORE overlay (best effort).
        if frame_f.shape[1] != w or frame_f.shape[0] != h:
            frame_f = cv2.resize(frame_f, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
        if frame_s.shape[1] != w or frame_s.shape[0] != h:
            frame_s = cv2.resize(frame_s, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)

        rows_t, idx_top = slice_rows(df_top, fr_top, idx_top, frame_idx)
        rows_f, idx_front = slice_rows(df_front, fr_front, idx_front, frame_idx)
        rows_s, idx_side = slice_rows(df_side, fr_side, idx_side, frame_idx)

        frame_t = overlay_frame(frame_t, rows_t, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_f = overlay_frame(frame_f, rows_f, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_s = overlay_frame(frame_s, rows_s, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)

        # Downsample professionally for each quadrant (INTER_AREA)
        top_small = cv2.resize(frame_t, (w_right, h_top), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        front_small = cv2.resize(frame_f, (w_right, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        side_small = cv2.resize(frame_s, (w_left, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)

        canvas = np.zeros((h, w, 3), dtype=np.uint8)
        # top-right
        canvas[0:h_top, w_left:w] = top_small
        # bottom-left
        canvas[h_top:h, 0:w_left] = side_small
        # bottom-right
        canvas[h_top:h, w_left:w] = front_small

        writer.write(canvas)
        frame_idx += 1

    top_cap.release()
    front_cap.release()
    side_cap.release()
    writer.release()


# -----------------------------
# CLI
# -----------------------------
def build_arg_parser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(prog=\"overlay_dlc_on_videos_v2.py\")
    p.add_argument(\"--dlc\", required=True, help=\"Path to dlc_long.csv\")

    p.add_argument(\"--topIn\", required=True, help=\"Input top camera video\")
    p.add_argument(\"--frontIn\", required=True, help=\"Input front camera video\")
    p.add_argument(\"--sideIn\", required=True, help=\"Input side camera video\")

    p.add_argument(\"--topOut\", required=True, help=\"Output annotated top video\")
    p.add_argument(\"--frontOut\", required=True, help=\"Output annotated front video\")
    p.add_argument(\"--sideOut\", required=True, help=\"Output annotated side video\")

    p.add_argument(\"--joinedVideo\", default=None,
                   help=\"Optional output path for a joined mosaic video (same resolution as inputs).\")

    p.add_argument(\"--topCam\", default=\"cam1_top\", help=\"Camera name in CSV for top view (default cam1_top)\")
    p.add_argument(\"--frontCam\", default=\"cam2_front\", help=\"Camera name in CSV for front view (default cam2_front)\")
    p.add_argument(\"--sideCam\", default=\"cam3_side\", help=\"Camera name in CSV for side view (default cam3_side)\")

    p.add_argument(\"--template\", default=None, help=\"Optional template file to draw skeleton edges ([EDGES] section)\")

    p.add_argument(\"--likelihood-min\", type=float, default=0.2, help=\"Only draw points with likelihood >= this (default 0.2)\")
    p.add_argument(\"--draw-labels\", action=\"store_true\", help=\"Draw text labels 'mouse:bodypart' near each point\")
    p.add_argument(\"--label-scale\", type=float, default=0.4, help=\"OpenCV font scale for labels (default 0.4)\")
    p.add_argument(\"--label-thickness\", type=int, default=1, help=\"Label thickness (default 1)\")
    p.add_argument(\"--force-fps\", type=float, default=None, help=\"Override output FPS (else use input video FPS)\")

    return p


def main() -> int:
    args = build_arg_parser().parse_args()

    df = pd.read_csv(args.dlc)
    required = {\"frame\", \"camera\", \"individual\", \"bodypart\", \"x\", \"y\", \"likelihood\"}
    missing = required - set(df.columns)
    if missing:
        raise ValueError(f\"dlc CSV missing columns: {sorted(missing)}\")

    edges = None
    if args.template:
        edges = parse_edges_from_template(args.template)
        if not edges:
            print(\"[warn] Template provided but no edges found; drawing only points.\")

    def df_for_cam(cam_name: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
        d = df[df[\"camera\"].astype(str) == str(cam_name)][[\"frame\", \"individual\", \"bodypart\", \"x\", \"y\", \"likelihood\"]].copy()
        # Ensure types are sane
        d[\"frame\"] = d[\"frame\"].astype(int)
        return d

    print(\"Loading DLC rows...\")
    df_top = df_for_cam(args.topCam)
    df_front = df_for_cam(args.frontCam)
    df_side = df_for_cam(args.sideCam)
    print(f\"Rows per view: top={len(df_top)}, front={len(df_front)}, side={len(df_side)}\")

    print(\"Annotating top video...\")
    overlay_video(args.topIn, args.topOut, df_top, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f\"Wrote: {args.topOut}\")

    print(\"Annotating front video...\")
    overlay_video(args.frontIn, args.frontOut, df_front, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f\"Wrote: {args.frontOut}\")

    print(\"Annotating side video...\")
    overlay_video(args.sideIn, args.sideOut, df_side, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f\"Wrote: {args.sideOut}\")

    if args.joinedVideo:
        print(\"Writing joined mosaic video...\")
        overlay_three_and_join(
            args.topIn, args.frontIn, args.sideIn,
            args.joinedVideo,
            df_top, df_front, df_side,
            edges=edges,
            likelihood_min=args.likelihood_min,
            draw_labels=args.draw_labels,
            label_scale=args.label_scale,
            label_thickness=args.label_thickness,
            force_fps=args.force_fps,
        )
        print(f\"Wrote: {args.joinedVideo}\")

    return 0


if __name__ == \"__main__\":
    raise SystemExit(main())
"""

User: For the correction of mouse identity the following conditions are important:

- There are always two mice. Mouse 0 has brownish fur. For mouse 1 the red and blue channels of the fur are exchanged such that it looks blueish.
- In your plot you are using a white skeleton for mouse 0 and a greenish skeleton for mouse 1.
- In principle it should be possible to for each body part extract from the image whether the fur at the body part is brown(ish) or blue(ish). However, it is not really trivial because in the environment of the position there are also all kinds of background colors. Sometimes, in particular at the tail-tip, there is hardly any fur.

So in an automatic correction,

First the average fur colors have to be identified. May be on a few frames that show the mice clearly separate from each other.

Then for each body part of each mouse in each frame it needs to be tried to identify the fur’s color. I.e. the question needs to be answered whether around the parts position there are at least a few pixels that belong to mouse 0 and - hopefully - not to mouse 1. Or the other way round. If this is the case, the body part can be assigned a mouse ID. If it is not obvious, it is better to leave the ID unassigned.

User: In the third step, it needs to be checked whether the majorities of the color-based part IDs agree with the ID assigned in the DLC_long.csv file. If not an ID change is required.

code = r"""#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
code += r'''
"""
overlay_dlc_on_videos_v3.py

Extends overlay_dlc_on_videos_v2.py with automatic, color-based identity correction.

Problem:
- In dlc_long.csv, identities can flip between two mice, and even individual body parts
  can occasionally be assigned to the wrong mouse.

Assumptions:
- Always exactly 2 mice.
- Mouse 0 fur is brown-ish (typically R > B).
- Mouse 1 fur is blue-ish (typically B > R) because red/blue channels were swapped.

Approach (per camera):
1) Estimate the two fur color prototypes from frames where mice are well separated
   (auto-picked by large centroid distance). Use k=2 clustering on median patch colors.
   The cluster with mean(R) > mean(B) is "brown" (mouse 0); the other is "blue" (mouse 1).
2) For each detection row, sample a small patch around (x,y) in the corresponding video frame.
   If enough pixels are close to either prototype, assign a color-based mouse ID (0/1).
   Otherwise leave unassigned.
3) For each frame, if the majority of assigned color-IDs disagree with the current mouse IDs,
   flip the mapping for that frame (frame-level swap).
4) For individual body-part rows that still contradict the color assignment:
   - If both mice's same body part are confidently swapped -> swap them.
   - If only one wants to move but the target already has that body part -> drop the leaving row
     (recommended by user to avoid confusion).
   - If target does not have it -> reassign to the other mouse.

Outputs:
- Annotated top/front/side videos (as before)
- Optional joined mosaic video (--joinedVideo)
- Optional corrected DLC CSV written to --dlcOut (same schema as input CSV)

Dependencies:
- numpy, pandas, opencv (cv2)

Usage (example):
  python overlay_dlc_on_videos_v3.py \
    --dlc ../dlc_long.csv \
    --topIn top.mp4 --frontIn front.mp4 --sideIn side.mp4 \
    --topOut top_anno.mp4 --frontOut front_anno.mp4 --sideOut side_anno.mp4 \
    --joinedVideo joined_anno.mp4 \
    --template ../mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
    --likelihood-min 0.2 \
    --autoCorrect \
    --dlcOut ../dlc_long_corrected.csv
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import cv2


# -----------------------------
# Template edges (optional)
# -----------------------------
def parse_edges_from_template(path: str | Path) -> List[Tuple[str, str]]:
    p = Path(path)
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]] = []
    in_edges = False
    for line in p.read_text(encoding="utf-8").splitlines():
        s = line.strip()
        if not s:
            continue
        if s.upper() == "[EDGES]":
            in_edges = True
            continue
        if s.startswith("[") and s.endswith("]") and s.upper() != "[EDGES]":
            in_edges = False
        if in_edges:
            parts = s.split()
            if len(parts) == 2:
                edges.append((parts[0], parts[1]))
    return edges


# -----------------------------
# Drawing helpers
# -----------------------------
def make_color_map(individuals: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Tuple[int, int, int]]:
    colors = [
        (255, 255, 255),  # white
        (80, 220, 80),    # green-ish
        (220, 80, 80),
        (80, 80, 220),
        (220, 220, 80),
        (220, 80, 220),
    ]
    return {ind: colors[i % len(colors)] for i, ind in enumerate(individuals)}


def overlay_frame(
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    rows: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
) -> np.ndarray:
    if rows.empty:
        return frame_bgr

    inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
    cmap = make_color_map(inds)

    coords: Dict[Tuple[str, str], Tuple[float, float, float]] = {}
    for r in rows.itertuples(index=False):
        ind = str(r.individual)
        bp = str(r.bodypart)
        x = float(r.x) if pd.notna(r.x) else np.nan
        y = float(r.y) if pd.notna(r.y) else np.nan
        lik = float(r.likelihood) if pd.notna(r.likelihood) else 0.0
        coords[(ind, bp)] = (x, y, lik)

    # skeleton
    if edges:
        for ind in inds:
            col = cmap[ind]
            for a, b in edges:
                ka, kb = (ind, a), (ind, b)
                if ka not in coords or kb not in coords:
                    continue
                xa, ya, la = coords[ka]
                xb, yb, lb = coords[kb]
                if la < likelihood_min or lb < likelihood_min:
                    continue
                if not (np.isfinite(xa) and np.isfinite(ya) and np.isfinite(xb) and np.isfinite(yb)):
                    continue
                cv2.line(frame_bgr, (int(xa), int(ya)), (int(xb), int(yb)), col, 2, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # points
    for ind in inds:
        col = cmap[ind]
        for (i_ind, bp), (x, y, lik) in coords.items():
            if i_ind != ind:
                continue
            if lik < likelihood_min:
                continue
            if not (np.isfinite(x) and np.isfinite(y)):
                continue
            cv2.circle(frame_bgr, (int(x), int(y)), 4, col, -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
            if draw_labels:
                cv2.putText(
                    frame_bgr,
                    f"{ind}:{bp}",
                    (int(x) + 6, int(y) - 6),
                    cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX,
                    float(label_scale),
                    col,
                    int(label_thickness),
                    cv2.LINE_AA,
                )
    return frame_bgr


# -----------------------------
# Video overlay (single)
# -----------------------------
def overlay_video(
    in_path: str | Path,
    out_path: str | Path,
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> Tuple[int, int, float, int]:
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(in_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open input video: {in_path}")

    w = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(out_path), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open output video: {out_path}")

    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)
    idx = 0

    frame_idx = 0
    written = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1

        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]
        out_frame = overlay_frame(frame, rows, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        writer.write(out_frame)
        frame_idx += 1
        written += 1

    cap.release()
    writer.release()
    return w, h, fps, written


# -----------------------------
# Joined mosaic writer
# -----------------------------
def overlay_three_and_join(
    top_in: str | Path, front_in: str | Path, side_in: str | Path,
    joined_out: str | Path,
    df_top: pd.DataFrame, df_front: pd.DataFrame, df_side: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    top_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(top_in))
    front_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(front_in))
    side_cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(side_in))
    if not top_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open top input video: {top_in}")
    if not front_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open front input video: {front_in}")
    if not side_cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open side input video: {side_in}")

    w = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(top_cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    w_left = w // 2
    w_right = w - w_left
    h_top = h // 2
    h_bottom = h - h_top

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(joined_out), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open joined output video: {joined_out}")

    def prep(df_cam: pd.DataFrame):
        df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
        return df_cam, df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)

    df_top, fr_top = prep(df_top)
    df_front, fr_front = prep(df_front)
    df_side, fr_side = prep(df_side)
    idx_top = idx_front = idx_side = 0

    def slice_rows(df_cam, fr_arr, idx, frame_idx):
        n = len(fr_arr)
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < n and fr_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]
        return rows, idx

    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok_t, frame_t = top_cap.read()
        ok_f, frame_f = front_cap.read()
        ok_s, frame_s = side_cap.read()
        if not (ok_t and ok_f and ok_s):
            break

        if frame_f.shape[1] != w or frame_f.shape[0] != h:
            frame_f = cv2.resize(frame_f, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
        if frame_s.shape[1] != w or frame_s.shape[0] != h:
            frame_s = cv2.resize(frame_s, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)

        rows_t, idx_top = slice_rows(df_top, fr_top, idx_top, frame_idx)
        rows_f, idx_front = slice_rows(df_front, fr_front, idx_front, frame_idx)
        rows_s, idx_side = slice_rows(df_side, fr_side, idx_side, frame_idx)

        frame_t = overlay_frame(frame_t, rows_t, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_f = overlay_frame(frame_f, rows_f, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)
        frame_s = overlay_frame(frame_s, rows_s, edges, likelihood_min, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)

        top_small = cv2.resize(frame_t, (w_right, h_top), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        front_small = cv2.resize(frame_f, (w_right, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        side_small = cv2.resize(frame_s, (w_left, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)

        canvas = np.zeros((h, w, 3), dtype=np.uint8)
        canvas[0:h_top, w_left:w] = top_small
        canvas[h_top:h, 0:w_left] = side_small
        canvas[h_top:h, w_left:w] = front_small

        writer.write(canvas)
        frame_idx += 1

    top_cap.release()
    front_cap.release()
    side_cap.release()
    writer.release()


# -----------------------------
# Color-based identity correction
# -----------------------------
def _parse_mouse_id(individual: str) -> Optional[int]:
    s = str(individual)
    digits = "".join([c for c in s if c.isdigit()])
    if digits == "":
        return None
    try:
        return int(digits)
    except Exception:
        return None


def _kmeans2(points: np.ndarray, iters: int = 15) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Very small kmeans for k=2.
    points: (N,3) float
    returns (centers (2,3), labels (N,))
    """
    if len(points) < 2:
        raise ValueError("Need at least 2 points for kmeans2.")
    # init: farthest pair
    # pick first, then farthest from it, then farthest from second
    p0 = points[0]
    d = np.sum((points - p0)**2, axis=1)
    c1 = points[int(np.argmax(d))]
    d2 = np.sum((points - c1)**2, axis=1)
    c0 = points[int(np.argmax(d2))]
    centers = np.stack([c0, c1], axis=0).astype(np.float64)

    for _ in range(iters):
        dist0 = np.sum((points - centers[0])**2, axis=1)
        dist1 = np.sum((points - centers[1])**2, axis=1)
        labels = (dist1 < dist0).astype(np.int32)
        # update
        for k in (0, 1):
            sel = points[labels == k]
            if len(sel) > 0:
                centers[k] = np.mean(sel, axis=0)
    return centers, labels


def _pick_separation_frames(df_cam: pd.DataFrame, min_lik: float, k: int) -> List[int]:
    """
    Choose up to k frames where the two individuals are far apart (centroid distance).
    """
    # Only use likely points
    d = df_cam[df_cam["likelihood"] >= min_lik]
    if d.empty:
        return []

    # ensure numeric mouse ids for individuals; keep only ids 0 and 1 if possible
    d = d.copy()
    d["mouse_id"] = d["individual"].astype(str).map(_parse_mouse_id)
    # if parse fails, use stable ordering
    if d["mouse_id"].isna().any():
        inds = sorted(d["individual"].astype(str).unique().tolist())
        mapping = {inds[i]: i for i in range(len(inds))}
        d["mouse_id"] = d["individual"].astype(str).map(mapping)

    # centroids per (frame, mouse_id)
    g = d.groupby(["frame", "mouse_id"])[["x", "y"]].mean().reset_index()
    # pivot to have x0,y0,x1,y1
    g0 = g[g["mouse_id"] == 0].set_index("frame")
    g1 = g[g["mouse_id"] == 1].set_index("frame")
    frames = sorted(list(set(g0.index).intersection(set(g1.index))))
    if not frames:
        return []
    dist = []
    for fr in frames:
        dx = float(g0.loc[fr, "x"] - g1.loc[fr, "x"])
        dy = float(g0.loc[fr, "y"] - g1.loc[fr, "y"])
        dist.append((fr, (dx*dx + dy*dy) ** 0.5))
    dist.sort(key=lambda t: t[1], reverse=True)
    return [int(fr) for fr, _ in dist[:k]]


def _median_patch_color(frame_bgr: np.ndarray, x: float, y: float, r: int) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    if not (np.isfinite(x) and np.isfinite(y)):
        return None
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    xi, yi = int(round(x)), int(round(y))
    x0 = max(0, xi - r)
    x1 = min(W, xi + r + 1)
    y0 = max(0, yi - r)
    y1 = min(H, yi + r + 1)
    patch = frame_bgr[y0:y1, x0:x1]
    if patch.size == 0:
        return None
    pix = patch.reshape(-1, 3).astype(np.float64)
    return np.median(pix, axis=0)  # BGR median


def _assign_color_id_from_patch(
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    x: float, y: float,
    r: int,
    centers_bgr: np.ndarray,  # (2,3)
    dist_thresh: float,
    min_frac: float,
    min_pixels: int,
    dominance: float,
) -> Tuple[int, float]:
    """
    Returns (assigned_id in {0,1,-1}, confidence)
    assigned_id corresponds to:
      0 -> brown cluster
      1 -> blue cluster
    """
    if not (np.isfinite(x) and np.isfinite(y)):
        return -1, 0.0
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    xi, yi = int(round(x)), int(round(y))
    x0 = max(0, xi - r)
    x1 = min(W, xi + r + 1)
    y0 = max(0, yi - r)
    y1 = min(H, yi + r + 1)
    patch = frame_bgr[y0:y1, x0:x1]
    if patch.size == 0:
        return -1, 0.0
    pix = patch.reshape(-1, 3).astype(np.float64)
    n = pix.shape[0]
    if n < min_pixels:
        return -1, 0.0

    thr2 = float(dist_thresh) ** 2
    d0 = np.sum((pix - centers_bgr[0])**2, axis=1)
    d1 = np.sum((pix - centers_bgr[1])**2, axis=1)
    c0 = int(np.sum(d0 <= thr2))
    c1 = int(np.sum(d1 <= thr2))
    best = 0 if c0 >= c1 else 1
    bestc = max(c0, c1)
    otherc = min(c0, c1)

    frac = bestc / max(1, n)
    if frac < min_frac:
        return -1, 0.0
    # dominance: require best to beat other by some margin (relative)
    if bestc < otherc * (1.0 + dominance) and (bestc - otherc) < 5:
        return -1, 0.0
    conf = (bestc - otherc) / max(1, n)
    return int(best), float(conf)


def correct_identities_for_camera(
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    video_path: str | Path,
    sep_lik: float,
    calib_frames: int,
    patch_radius: int,
    calib_lik: float,
    dist_thresh: float,
    min_frac: float,
    min_pixels: int,
    dominance: float,
    vote_lik: float,
    drop_on_conflict: bool,
) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Return a corrected copy of df_cam for a single camera (contains only that camera's rows).
    """
    if df_cam.empty:
        return df_cam

    df_cam = df_cam.copy()
    df_cam["frame"] = df_cam["frame"].astype(int)

    # Normalize individual ids to 0/1 if possible
    df_cam["mouse_id"] = df_cam["individual"].astype(str).map(_parse_mouse_id)
    if df_cam["mouse_id"].isna().any():
        inds = sorted(df_cam["individual"].astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) != 2:
            raise ValueError(f"Expected 2 individuals, found {inds}")
        mapping = {inds[0]: 0, inds[1]: 1}
        df_cam["mouse_id"] = df_cam["individual"].astype(str).map(mapping)

    # Pick calibration frames (separated mice)
    frames_calib = _pick_separation_frames(df_cam, min_lik=sep_lik, k=calib_frames)
    if len(frames_calib) < 3:
        print("[autoCorrect] Not enough separation frames found; skipping correction for this camera.")
        return df_cam.drop(columns=["mouse_id"], errors="ignore")

    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(video_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open video for correction: {video_path}")

    # Build a fast per-frame slice index
    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values(["frame"]).reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)

    # Step 1: gather patch medians in calibration frames
    # Exclude tail_tip by default (often low-fur)
    exclude_bps = {"tail_tip"}
    samples = []
    frame_set = set(frames_calib)

    idx = 0
    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break
        if frame_idx > max(frames_calib):
            break

        if frame_idx in frame_set:
            # slice rows for this frame
            while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
                idx += 1
            start = idx
            while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
                idx += 1
            if idx > start:
                rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx]
                rows = rows[(rows["likelihood"] >= calib_lik) & (~rows["bodypart"].astype(str).isin(exclude_bps))]
                for r in rows.itertuples(index=False):
                    c = _median_patch_color(frame, float(r.x), float(r.y), patch_radius)
                    if c is not None and np.all(np.isfinite(c)):
                        samples.append(c)
        frame_idx += 1

    cap.release()

    if len(samples) < 20:
        print("[autoCorrect] Not enough color samples; skipping correction for this camera.")
        return df_cam.drop(columns=["mouse_id"], errors="ignore")

    samples = np.stack(samples, axis=0)

    # kmeans into two clusters in BGR space
    centers, labels = _kmeans2(samples, iters=20)

    # Decide which center is brown vs blue:
    # Brown cluster: R > B (in BGR, channel2 > channel0)
    # Ensure centers_bgr[0] is brown and centers_bgr[1] is blue
    brown_idx = 0 if centers[0, 2] >= centers[0, 0] else 1
    blue_idx = 1 - brown_idx
    centers_bgr = np.stack([centers[brown_idx], centers[blue_idx]], axis=0)

    print(f"[autoCorrect] Color prototypes (BGR): brown~{centers_bgr[0].round(1).tolist()}  blue~{centers_bgr[1].round(1).tolist()}")

    # Step 2: compute color-based assignment per row (needs scanning video again)
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(video_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open video for correction (pass2): {video_path}")

    df_cam["color_id"] = -1
    df_cam["color_conf"] = 0.0

    idx = 0
    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        if idx > start:
            # operate on row indices [start, idx)
            sub = df_cam.iloc[start:idx]
            for ridx, r in zip(range(start, idx), sub.itertuples(index=False)):
                if float(r.likelihood) < vote_lik:
                    continue
                cid, conf = _assign_color_id_from_patch(
                    frame_bgr=frame,
                    x=float(r.x), y=float(r.y),
                    r=patch_radius,
                    centers_bgr=centers_bgr,
                    dist_thresh=dist_thresh,
                    min_frac=min_frac,
                    min_pixels=min_pixels,
                    dominance=dominance,
                )
                if cid != -1:
                    df_cam.at[ridx, "color_id"] = cid
                    df_cam.at[ridx, "color_conf"] = conf

        frame_idx += 1

    cap.release()

    # Step 3: per-frame swap decision based on majority vote
    # Compute votes only where color_id assigned and likelihood >= vote_lik
    df_vote = df_cam[(df_cam["color_id"] >= 0) & (df_cam["likelihood"] >= vote_lik)]
    if df_vote.empty:
        print("[autoCorrect] No color votes available; skipping correction for this camera.")
        return df_cam.drop(columns=["mouse_id"], errors="ignore")

    # For each frame, score "no swap" vs "swap"
    # no swap consistent if color_id == mouse_id
    # swap consistent if color_id == 1 - mouse_id
    g = df_vote.groupby("frame").apply(
        lambda x: pd.Series({
            "score_noswap": int(np.sum(x["color_id"].to_numpy() == x["mouse_id"].to_numpy())),
            "score_swap": int(np.sum(x["color_id"].to_numpy() == (1 - x["mouse_id"].to_numpy()))),
        })
    ).reset_index()

    swap_frames = set(g[g["score_swap"] > g["score_noswap"]]["frame"].astype(int).tolist())
    if len(swap_frames) > 0:
        print(f"[autoCorrect] Frame-level swaps selected: {len(swap_frames)} frames (out of {df_cam['frame'].nunique()}).")

    df_cam["mouse_id_corr"] = df_cam["mouse_id"].astype(int)
    mask_swap = df_cam["frame"].isin(swap_frames)
    df_cam.loc[mask_swap, "mouse_id_corr"] = 1 - df_cam.loc[mask_swap, "mouse_id_corr"]

    # Step 4: body-part-level corrections with conflict handling
    # Build per (frame, bodypart) groups
    keep_rows = np.ones(len(df_cam), dtype=bool)

    # We'll process only rows where color_id assigned (>=0)
    df_idx = df_cam.reset_index(drop=False).rename(columns={"index": "row_idx"})
    grouped = df_idx.groupby(["frame", "bodypart"])

    for (fr, bp), grp in grouped:
        # only consider if any has a confident color assignment
        grp_assigned = grp[grp["color_id"] >= 0]
        if grp_assigned.empty:
            continue
        # We expect max 2 rows (two mice) but allow more and handle by selecting top likelihood per mouse_id_corr
        # Keep at most one per corrected mouse for this bodypart
        chosen = []
        for mid in (0, 1):
            sub = grp[grp["mouse_id_corr"] == mid]
            if sub.empty:
                continue
            # choose highest likelihood row for this mid
            chosen.append(sub.sort_values("likelihood", ascending=False).iloc[0])
        grp2 = pd.DataFrame(chosen)

        if grp2.empty:
            continue

        # Create dict mid->row
        rows_by_mid = {int(r["mouse_id_corr"]): r for _, r in grp2.iterrows()}

        # Determine desired mid from color assignment, if any
        desired = {}
        for mid, r in rows_by_mid.items():
            if int(r["color_id"]) >= 0:
                desired[mid] = int(r["color_id"])

        if len(rows_by_mid) == 2:
            r0 = rows_by_mid[0]
            r1 = rows_by_mid[1]
            d0 = desired.get(0, None)
            d1 = desired.get(1, None)

            # case: both confidently want to swap (0->1 and 1->0)
            if d0 == 1 and d1 == 0:
                # swap corrected ids for these two rows
                i0 = int(r0["row_idx"])
                i1 = int(r1["row_idx"])
                df_cam.at[i0, "mouse_id_corr"] = 1
                df_cam.at[i1, "mouse_id_corr"] = 0
                continue

        # Otherwise handle each row independently
        for mid, r in rows_by_mid.items():
            dmid = desired.get(mid, None)
            if dmid is None:
                continue
            if dmid == mid:
                continue  # consistent

            # wants to move to dmid
            if dmid not in rows_by_mid:
                # target missing -> reassign
                df_cam.at[int(r["row_idx"]), "mouse_id_corr"] = dmid
            else:
                # target exists -> conflict
                if drop_on_conflict:
                    keep_rows[int(r["row_idx"])] = False
                # else: do nothing

    df_cam = df_cam[keep_rows].copy()

    # Rebuild individual labels to match corrected mouse ids.
    # Preserve original naming pattern if possible.
    inds = sorted(df_cam["individual"].astype(str).unique().tolist())
    # Try to infer "mouse0"/"mouse1"
    def make_name(mid: int) -> str:
        # if original names contain "mouse", keep it
        for s in inds:
            if "mouse" in s.lower():
                prefix = "".join([c for c in s if not c.isdigit()])
                if prefix == "":
                    prefix = "mouse"
                return f"{prefix}{mid}"
        return f"mouse{mid}"

    df_cam["individual"] = df_cam["mouse_id_corr"].astype(int).map(lambda m: make_name(int(m)))

    return df_cam.drop(columns=["mouse_id", "mouse_id_corr"], errors="ignore")


# -----------------------------
# Main
# -----------------------------
def build_arg_parser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(prog="overlay_dlc_on_videos_v3.py")
    p.add_argument("--dlc", required=True, help="Path to dlc_long.csv")

    p.add_argument("--topIn", required=True, help="Input top camera video")
    p.add_argument("--frontIn", required=True, help="Input front camera video")
    p.add_argument("--sideIn", required=True, help="Input side camera video")

    p.add_argument("--topOut", required=True, help="Output annotated top video")
    p.add_argument("--frontOut", required=True, help="Output annotated front video")
    p.add_argument("--sideOut", required=True, help="Output annotated side video")

    p.add_argument("--joinedVideo", default=None,
                   help="Optional output path for a joined mosaic video (same resolution as inputs).")

    p.add_argument("--topCam", default="cam1_top", help="Camera name in CSV for top view (default cam1_top)")
    p.add_argument("--frontCam", default="cam2_front", help="Camera name in CSV for front view (default cam2_front)")
    p.add_argument("--sideCam", default="cam3_side", help="Camera name in CSV for side view (default cam3_side)")

    p.add_argument("--template", default=None, help="Optional template file to draw skeleton edges ([EDGES] section)")

    p.add_argument("--likelihood-min", type=float, default=0.2, help="Only draw points with likelihood >= this (default 0.2)")
    p.add_argument("--draw-labels", action="store_true", help="Draw text labels 'mouse:bodypart' near each point")
    p.add_argument("--label-scale", type=float, default=0.4, help="OpenCV font scale for labels (default 0.4)")
    p.add_argument("--label-thickness", type=int, default=1, help="Label thickness (default 1)")
    p.add_argument("--force-fps", type=float, default=None, help="Override output FPS (else use input video FPS)")

    # Identity correction options
    p.add_argument("--autoCorrect", action="store_true", help="Enable color-based identity correction (2 mice).")
    p.add_argument("--dlcOut", default=None, help="Optional output path for corrected dlc CSV.")
    p.add_argument("--sep-likelihood", type=float, default=0.7,
                   help="Likelihood threshold used to find well-separated frames (default 0.7).")
    p.add_argument("--calib-frames", type=int, default=25,
                   help="Number of separation frames used to estimate fur colors (default 25).")
    p.add_argument("--calib-likelihood", type=float, default=0.85,
                   help="Likelihood threshold for using detections in color calibration (default 0.85).")
    p.add_argument("--vote-likelihood", type=float, default=0.5,
                   help="Likelihood threshold for color voting/correction (default 0.5).")
    p.add_argument("--patch-radius", type=int, default=6,
                   help="Patch radius (pixels) around each detection (default 6 -> 13x13).")
    p.add_argument("--color-dist", type=float, default=35.0,
                   help="Color distance threshold in BGR space for counting fur pixels (default 35).")
    p.add_argument("--min-fur-frac", type=float, default=0.08,
                   help="Minimum fraction of patch pixels close to a prototype to accept assignment (default 0.08).")
    p.add_argument("--min-pixels", type=int, default=30,
                   help="Minimum patch pixel count required (default 30).")
    p.add_argument("--dominance", type=float, default=0.25,
                   help="Dominance margin for best cluster count vs second best (default 0.25).")
    p.add_argument("--drop-on-conflict", action="store_true",
                   help="When a part wants to switch but the target already has that part, drop the leaving part.")

    return p


def main() -> int:
    args = build_arg_parser().parse_args()

    df = pd.read_csv(args.dlc)
    required = {"frame", "camera", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"}
    missing = required - set(df.columns)
    if missing:
        raise ValueError(f"dlc CSV missing columns: {sorted(missing)}")

    edges = None
    if args.template:
        edges = parse_edges_from_template(args.template)
        if not edges:
            print("[warn] Template provided but no edges found; drawing only points.")

    def df_for_cam(cam_name: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
        d = df[df["camera"].astype(str) == str(cam_name)].copy()
        d["frame"] = d["frame"].astype(int)
        return d

    print("Loading DLC rows...")
    df_top = df_for_cam(args.topCam)
    df_front = df_for_cam(args.frontCam)
    df_side = df_for_cam(args.sideCam)
    print(f"Rows per view: top={len(df_top)}, front={len(df_front)}, side={len(df_side)}")

    if args.autoCorrect:
        print("\n[autoCorrect] Correcting identities for top view...")
        df_top = correct_identities_for_camera(
            df_top, args.topIn,
            sep_lik=float(args.sep_likelihood),
            calib_frames=int(args.calib_frames),
            patch_radius=int(args.patch_radius),
            calib_lik=float(args.calib_likelihood),
            dist_thresh=float(args.color_dist),
            min_frac=float(args.min_fur_frac),
            min_pixels=int(args.min_pixels),
            dominance=float(args.dominance),
            vote_lik=float(args.vote_likelihood),
            drop_on_conflict=bool(args.drop_on_conflict),
        )
        print("[autoCorrect] Correcting identities for front view...")
        df_front = correct_identities_for_camera(
            df_front, args.frontIn,
            sep_lik=float(args.sep_likelihood),
            calib_frames=int(args.calib_frames),
            patch_radius=int(args.patch_radius),
            calib_lik=float(args.calib_likelihood),
            dist_thresh=float(args.color_dist),
            min_frac=float(args.min_fur_frac),
            min_pixels=int(args.min_pixels),
            dominance=float(args.dominance),
            vote_lik=float(args.vote_likelihood),
            drop_on_conflict=bool(args.drop_on_conflict),
        )
        print("[autoCorrect] Correcting identities for side view...")
        df_side = correct_identities_for_camera(
            df_side, args.sideIn,
            sep_lik=float(args.sep_likelihood),
            calib_frames=int(args.calib_frames),
            patch_radius=int(args.patch_radius),
            calib_lik=float(args.calib_likelihood),
            dist_thresh=float(args.color_dist),
            min_frac=float(args.min_fur_frac),
            min_pixels=int(args.min_pixels),
            dominance=float(args.dominance),
            vote_lik=float(args.vote_likelihood),
            drop_on_conflict=bool(args.drop_on_conflict),
        )

        if args.dlcOut:
            # write corrected combined CSV (preserve other columns if present)
            # We'll update only the rows for these three cameras by matching (camera, frame, bodypart, x, y, likelihood) indices
            # Simpler: rebuild the concatenated corrected rows and keep any other cameras untouched.
            others = df[~df["camera"].astype(str).isin([args.topCam, args.frontCam, args.sideCam])].copy()
            out_df = pd.concat([others, df_top, df_front, df_side], ignore_index=True)
            out_df.to_csv(args.dlcOut, index=False)
            print(f"[autoCorrect] Wrote corrected DLC CSV: {args.dlcOut}")

    # For overlay we keep only the columns needed
    cols = ["frame", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"]
    df_top_ov = df_top[cols].copy()
    df_front_ov = df_front[cols].copy()
    df_side_ov = df_side[cols].copy()

    print("\nAnnotating top video...")
    overlay_video(args.topIn, args.topOut, df_top_ov, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.topOut}")

    print("Annotating front video...")
    overlay_video(args.frontIn, args.frontOut, df_front_ov, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.frontOut}")

    print("Annotating side video...")
    overlay_video(args.sideIn, args.sideOut, df_side_ov, edges, args.likelihood_min, args.draw_labels, args.label_scale, args.label_thickness, args.force_fps)
    print(f"Wrote: {args.sideOut}")

    if args.joinedVideo:
        print("Writing joined mosaic video...")
        overlay_three_and_join(
            args.topIn, args.frontIn, args.sideIn,
            args.joinedVideo,
            df_top_ov, df_front_ov, df_side_ov,
            edges=edges,
            likelihood_min=args.likelihood_min,
            draw_labels=args.draw_labels,
            label_scale=args.label_scale,
            label_thickness=args.label_thickness,
            force_fps=args.force_fps,
        )
        print(f"Wrote: {args.joinedVideo}")

    return 0


if __name__ == "__main__":
    raise SystemExit(main())

Assistant: from pathlib import Path

v2_path = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v2.py")
