        dist1 = np.sum((pts - centers[1]) ** 2, axis=1)
        labels = (dist1 < dist0).astype(np.int32)
        for k in (0, 1):

    dist0 = np.sum((pts - centers[0]) ** 2, axis=1)
    dist1 = np.sum((pts - centers[1]) ** 2, axis=1)
    labels = (dist1 < dist0).astype(np.int32)

def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(
    rows: pd.DataFrame,
    min_lik: float,
    use_dlc_ids: bool,
) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    """
    Return point prompts (2,2) in pixel coords (x,y) for the two mice.
    If use_dlc_ids: use current 'individual' labels and compute centroids.
    Else: ignore ids and kmeans-cluster all points into two clusters.
    """
    rows = rows[rows["likelihood"] >= min_lik]
    if len(rows) < 4:
        return None

    if use_dlc_ids:
        inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) < 2:
            return None
        inds = inds[:2]
        c = []
        for ind in inds:
            sub = rows[rows["individual"].astype(str) == ind]
            if len(sub) < 2:
                return None
            c.append([float(sub["x"].mean()), float(sub["y"].mean())])
        return np.array(c, dtype=np.float32)

    pts = rows[["x", "y"]].to_numpy(dtype=np.float64)
    try:
        centers, _ = _kmeans2_xy(pts, iters=25)
    except Exception:
        return None
    return centers.astype(np.float32)


def _sam_load_predictor(checkpoint: str, model_type: str, device: str):
    if not _HAS_SAM:
        raise RuntimeError(
            "segment_anything/torch not available. Install per https://github.com/facebookresearch/segment-anything "
            "and ensure torch is installed."
        )
    if device == "auto":
        device = "cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
    sam = sam_model_registry[model_type](checkpoint=checkpoint)
    sam.to(device=device)
    predictor = SamPredictor(sam)
    return predictor


def _sam_segment_two_mice(predictor, frame_bgr: np.ndarray, prompts_xy: np.ndarray, multimask: bool = True):
    """
    Returns (mask0, mask1) bool arrays shape (H,W).
    """
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    masks_out = []
    for i in range(2):
        p = prompts_xy[i].reshape(1, 2)
        labels = np.array([1], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(point_coords=p, point_labels=labels, multimask_output=bool(multimask))
        best = int(np.argmax(scores))
        masks_out.append(masks[best].astype(bool))
    return masks_out[0], masks_out[1]


def _overlay_masks_constant_color(frame_bgr: np.ndarray, mask0: np.ndarray, mask1: np.ndarray, alpha: float) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Fill each mask with its mean color and alpha-blend onto original.
    """
    out = frame_bgr.astype(np.float32)

    overlap = mask0 & mask1
    if overlap.any():
        if mask0.sum() >= mask1.sum():
            mask1 = mask1 & (~overlap)
        else:
            mask0 = mask0 & (~overlap)

    for mask in (mask0, mask1):
        if mask is None or mask.sum() == 0:
            continue
        pix = frame_bgr[mask]
        if pix.size == 0:
            continue
        mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float32)
        seg = out.copy()
        seg[mask] = mean_col
        out = (1.0 - alpha) * out + alpha * seg

    return np.clip(out, 0, 255).astype(np.uint8)


def overlay_video_with_sam(
    in_path: str | Path,
    out_path: str | Path,
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min_draw: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
    sam_checkpoint: str,
    sam_model_type: str,
    sam_device: str,
    sam_alpha: float,
    sam_min_lik: float,
    sam_use_dlc_ids: bool,
    sam_every: int,
    sam_only: bool,
) -> None:
    predictor = _sam_load_predictor(sam_checkpoint, sam_model_type, sam_device)

    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(in_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open input video: {in_path}")

    w = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(out_path), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open output video: {out_path}")

    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)
    idx = 0

    last_prompts = None
    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]

        out_frame = frame
        if sam_every <= 1 or (frame_idx % sam_every == 0):
            prompts = _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows, min_lik=sam_min_lik, use_dlc_ids=bool(sam_use_dlc_ids))
            if prompts is None:
                prompts = last_prompts
            else:
                last_prompts = prompts

            if prompts is not None:
                try:
                    m0, m1 = _sam_segment_two_mice(predictor, out_frame, prompts_xy=prompts, multimask=True)
                    out_frame = _overlay_masks_constant_color(out_frame, m0, m1, alpha=float(sam_alpha))
                    # draw prompt points (white/green)
                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[0, 0]), int(prompts[0, 1])), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[1, 0]), int(prompts[1, 1])), 4, (80, 220, 80), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
                except Exception:
                    pass

        if not sam_only:
            out_frame = overlay_frame(out_frame, rows, edges, likelihood_min_draw, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)

        writer.write(out_frame)
        frame_idx += 1

    cap.release()
    writer.release()


def join_quadrants_from_videos(
    top_video: str | Path,
    front_video: str | Path,
    side_video: str | Path,
    joined_out: str | Path,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    cap_t = cv2.VideoCapture(str(top_video))
    cap_f = cv2.VideoCapture(str(front_video))
    cap_s = cv2.VideoCapture(str(side_video))
    if not cap_t.isOpened() or not cap_f.isOpened() or not cap_s.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError("Could not open one of the annotated videos for joining.")

    w = int(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    w_left = w // 2
    w_right = w - w_left
    h_top = h // 2
    h_bottom = h - h_top

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(joined_out), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open joined output video: {joined_out}")

    while True:
        ok_t, ft = cap_t.read()
        ok_f, ff = cap_f.read()
        ok_s, fs = cap_s.read()
        if not (ok_t and ok_f and ok_s):
            break

        if ff.shape[1] != w or ff.shape[0] != h:
            ff = cv2.resize(ff, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
        if fs.shape[1] != w or fs.shape[0] != h:
            fs = cv2.resize(fs, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)

        top_small = cv2.resize(ft, (w_right, h_top), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        front_small = cv2.resize(ff, (w_right, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        side_small = cv2.resize(fs, (w_left, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)

        canvas = np.zeros((h, w, 3), dtype=np.uint8)
        canvas[0:h_top, w_left:w] = top_small
        canvas[h_top:h, 0:w_left] = side_small
        canvas[h_top:h, w_left:w] = front_small
        writer.write(canvas)

    cap_t.release()
    cap_f.release()
    cap_s.release()
    writer.release()
"""
code = code[:pos] + sam_helpers + "\n" + code[pos:]

sam_helpers = """
# -----------------------------
# SAM helpers (segmentation visualization)
# -----------------------------
def _kmeans2_xy(points_xy: np.ndarray, iters: int = 20) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    # KMeans k=2 in 2D. Returns (centers (2,2), labels (N,))
    if len(points_xy) < 2:
        raise ValueError("Need >=2 points for kmeans2_xy")
    pts = points_xy.astype(np.float64)
    p0 = pts[0]
    d = np.sum((pts - p0) ** 2, axis=1)
    c1 = pts[int(np.argmax(d))]
    d2 = np.sum((pts - c1) ** 2, axis=1)
    c0 = pts[int(np.argmax(d2))]
    centers = np.stack([c0, c1], axis=0).astype(np.float64)

    labels = np.zeros(len(pts), dtype=np.int32)
    for _ in range(iters):
        dist0 = np.sum((pts - centers[0]) ** 2, axis=1)
        dist1 = np.sum((pts - centers[1]) ** 2, axis=1)
        labels = (dist1 < dist0).astype(np.int32)
        for k in (0, 1):
            sel = pts[labels == k]
            if len(sel) > 0:
                centers[k] = np.mean(sel, axis=0)

    dist0 = np.sum((pts - centers[0]) ** 2, axis=1)
    dist1 = np.sum((pts - centers[1]) ** 2, axis=1)
    labels = (dist1 < dist0).astype(np.int32)
    return centers, labels


def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows: pd.DataFrame, min_lik: float, use_dlc_ids: bool) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    # Return point prompts (2,2) in pixel coords (x,y) for the two mice.
    rows = rows[rows["likelihood"] >= min_lik]
    if len(rows) < 4:
        return None

    if use_dlc_ids:
        inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) < 2:
            return None
        inds = inds[:2]
        c = []
        for ind in inds:
            sub = rows[rows["individual"].astype(str) == ind]
            if len(sub) < 2:
                return None
            c.append([float(sub["x"].mean()), float(sub["y"].mean())])
        return np.array(c, dtype=np.float32)

    pts = rows[["x", "y"]].to_numpy(dtype=np.float64)
    try:
        centers, _ = _kmeans2_xy(pts, iters=25)
    except Exception:
        return None
    return centers.astype(np.float32)


def _sam_load_predictor(checkpoint: str, model_type: str, device: str):
    if not _HAS_SAM:
        raise RuntimeError(
            "segment_anything/torch not available. Install per https://github.com/facebookresearch/segment-anything "
            "and ensure torch is installed."
        )
    if device == "auto":
        device = "cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
    sam = sam_model_registry[model_type](checkpoint=checkpoint)
    sam.to(device=device)
    predictor = SamPredictor(sam)
    return predictor


def _sam_segment_two_mice(predictor, frame_bgr: np.ndarray, prompts_xy: np.ndarray, multimask: bool = True):
    # Returns (mask0, mask1) bool arrays shape (H,W)
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    masks_out = []
    for i in range(2):
        p = prompts_xy[i].reshape(1, 2)
        labels = np.array([1], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(point_coords=p, point_labels=labels, multimask_output=bool(multimask))
        best = int(np.argmax(scores))
        masks_out.append(masks[best].astype(bool))
    return masks_out[0], masks_out[1]


def _overlay_masks_constant_color(frame_bgr: np.ndarray, mask0: np.ndarray, mask1: np.ndarray, alpha: float) -> np.ndarray:
    # Fill each mask with its mean color and alpha-blend onto original.
    out = frame_bgr.astype(np.float32)

    overlap = mask0 & mask1
    if overlap.any():
        if mask0.sum() >= mask1.sum():
            mask1 = mask1 & (~overlap)
        else:
            mask0 = mask0 & (~overlap)

    for mask in (mask0, mask1):
        if mask is None or mask.sum() == 0:
            continue
        pix = frame_bgr[mask]
        if pix.size == 0:
            continue
        mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float32)
        seg = out.copy()
        seg[mask] = mean_col
        out = (1.0 - alpha) * out + alpha * seg

    return np.clip(out, 0, 255).astype(np.uint8)


def overlay_video_with_sam(
    in_path: str | Path,
    out_path: str | Path,
    df_cam: pd.DataFrame,
    edges: Optional[List[Tuple[str, str]]],
    likelihood_min_draw: float,
    draw_labels: bool,
    label_scale: float,
    label_thickness: int,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
    sam_checkpoint: str,
    sam_model_type: str,
    sam_device: str,
    sam_alpha: float,
    sam_min_lik: float,
    sam_use_dlc_ids: bool,
    sam_every: int,
    sam_only: bool,
) -> None:
    predictor = _sam_load_predictor(sam_checkpoint, sam_model_type, sam_device)

    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(in_path))
    if not cap.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open input video: {in_path}")

    w = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(out_path), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open output video: {out_path}")

    df_cam = df_cam.sort_values("frame").reset_index(drop=True)
    frames_arr = df_cam["frame"].to_numpy(dtype=np.int64)
    nrows = len(df_cam)
    idx = 0

    last_prompts = None
    frame_idx = 0
    while True:
        ok, frame = cap.read()
        if not ok:
            break

        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] < frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        start = idx
        while idx < nrows and frames_arr[idx] == frame_idx:
            idx += 1
        rows = df_cam.iloc[start:idx] if idx > start else df_cam.iloc[0:0]

        out_frame = frame
        if sam_every <= 1 or (frame_idx % sam_every == 0):
            prompts = _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows, min_lik=sam_min_lik, use_dlc_ids=bool(sam_use_dlc_ids))
            if prompts is None:
                prompts = last_prompts
            else:
                last_prompts = prompts

            if prompts is not None:
                try:
                    m0, m1 = _sam_segment_two_mice(predictor, out_frame, prompts_xy=prompts, multimask=True)
                    out_frame = _overlay_masks_constant_color(out_frame, m0, m1, alpha=float(sam_alpha))
                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[0, 0]), int(prompts[0, 1])), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[1, 0]), int(prompts[1, 1])), 4, (80, 220, 80), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
                except Exception:
                    pass

        if not sam_only:
            out_frame = overlay_frame(out_frame, rows, edges, likelihood_min_draw, draw_labels, label_scale, label_thickness)

        writer.write(out_frame)
        frame_idx += 1

    cap.release()
    writer.release()


def join_quadrants_from_videos(
    top_video: str | Path,
    front_video: str | Path,
    side_video: str | Path,
    joined_out: str | Path,
    force_fps: Optional[float],
) -> None:
    # Create joined mosaic from already-rendered videos using INTER_AREA downsampling.
    cap_t = cv2.VideoCapture(str(top_video))
    cap_f = cv2.VideoCapture(str(front_video))
    cap_s = cv2.VideoCapture(str(side_video))
    if not cap_t.isOpened() or not cap_f.isOpened() or not cap_s.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError("Could not open one of the annotated videos for joining.")

    w = int(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH))
    h = int(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT))
    fps_in = float(cap_t.get(cv2.CAP_PROP_FPS))
    fps = float(force_fps) if force_fps is not None else (fps_in if fps_in > 1e-6 else 10.0)

    w_left = w // 2
    w_right = w - w_left
    h_top = h // 2
    h_bottom = h - h_top

    fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")
    writer = cv2.VideoWriter(str(joined_out), fourcc, fps, (w, h))
    if not writer.isOpened():
        raise RuntimeError(f"Could not open joined output video: {joined_out}")

    while True:
        ok_t, ft = cap_t.read()
        ok_f, ff = cap_f.read()
        ok_s, fs = cap_s.read()
        if not (ok_t and ok_f and ok_s):
            break

        if ff.shape[1] != w or ff.shape[0] != h:
            ff = cv2.resize(ff, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
        if fs.shape[1] != w or fs.shape[0] != h:
            fs = cv2.resize(fs, (w, h), interpolation=cv2.INTER_LINEAR)

        top_small = cv2.resize(ft, (w_right, h_top), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        front_small = cv2.resize(ff, (w_right, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)
        side_small = cv2.resize(fs, (w_left, h_bottom), interpolation=cv2.INTER_AREA)

        canvas = np.zeros((h, w, 3), dtype=np.uint8)
        canvas[0:h_top, w_left:w] = top_small
        canvas[h_top:h, 0:w_left] = side_small
        canvas[h_top:h, w_left:w] = front_small
        writer.write(canvas)

    cap_t.release()
    cap_f.release()
    cap_s.release()
    writer.release()
"""
code = code[:pos] + sam_helpers + "\n" + code[pos:]

# Add SAM CLI args after force-fps

Assistant: Yes — using **SAM (Segment Anything)** is a sensible next move, because your current color voting fails mostly due to *background contamination* around keypoints. With SAM, we can extract each mouse’s **actual pixel segment** first, then:

- visualize both mouse segments (each filled with its **mean BGR color**, constant inside the mask),
- and later (if you want) compute mouse identity from segment colors in a much cleaner way.

I implemented this as an updated script:

[Download overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py)

### What it does
If you pass `--sam`, for each frame and each camera view it:

1. computes two “mouse prompt points” near the mice:
   - default: **kmeans clustering in XY** over all DLC points (ignores IDs → robust against identity flips)
   - optional: `--sam-use-dlc-ids` uses DLC mouse IDs for prompts instead (not recommended right now)
2. runs SAM with those two point prompts to get two masks
3. fills each mask with the **average BGR color** inside that mask (constant color)
4. alpha-blends the constant-color masks onto the original frame
5. optionally overlays skeleton/points afterward (unless `--sam-only`)

It also generates the joined mosaic **from the already-rendered outputs** (so SAM isn’t recomputed again in the join step), with proper `INTER_AREA` downsampling.

---

## Dependencies you must install (SAM + torch)
This script uses Meta’s official SAM Python API (`sam_model_registry`, `SamPredictor`). The official installation method is via the GitHub repo. citeturn0search4

You need:
- `torch`, `torchvision`
- `segment_anything` (`pip install git+https://github.com/facebookresearch/segment-anything.git`)
- a SAM checkpoint file (`sam_vit_b_01ec64.pth`, `sam_vit_l_0b3195.pth`, or `sam_vit_h_4b8939.pth`) citeturn0search4

(For speed: `vit_b` is the best default.)


### Useful options
- `--sam-only`  
  renders only segments (no skeleton/points)
- `--sam-every 5`  
  runs SAM every 5 frames (much faster, still useful for debugging)
- `--sam-use-dlc-ids`  
  uses DLC IDs for prompt centroids (I’d avoid it for now)

## Why this should help
Your previous method tried to infer fur color from local patches around keypoints. That fails because the patch often contains:
- background pixels,
- the other mouse,
- low-fur regions (tail tip),
- motion blur / occlusions.

SAM instead extracts the whole mouse region, so the mean color inside the segment is dramatically more stable.

then the next step is straightforward: use the **segment mean color** per frame to assign mouse0/mouse1 robustly (and optionally propagate identities temporally).

User: What exactly did you implement? Is it correct that

- the given body parts are averaged (center of gravity)
- the sam segment including that center of  gravity is computed
- the color of the segment's pixels is replaced by some local average (or something similar, but not a constant color)
- a filled circle in white and green is set to the center of gravity for mouse0 and mouse 1

?

Assistant: Yes — that’s essentially what’s implemented, with a couple of important specifics:

- **Prompt computation (center of gravity):**
  - For each frame, it takes the DLC detections in that camera view with `likelihood >= --sam-min-likelihood`.
  - It then computes **two prompt points** (2×(x,y)):
    - **Default (recommended right now):** it **ignores DLC IDs** and runs **k-means (k=2) in XY** over *all* those detections, and uses the **two cluster centroids** as the two prompts.
    - If you pass `--sam-use-dlc-ids`, then it instead computes **one centroid per DLC individual** (mouse0/mouse1 as labeled in the CSV).

- **SAM segmentation:**
  - For each of the two prompt points, it calls SAM with a **single positive point prompt** (`point_labels=[1]`).
  - SAM may return multiple candidate masks (multimask); the code picks the **highest-score mask** for each prompt.
  - There is **no special “segment that contains the centroid” selection step**, because SAM is *already being asked* to segment the object at that point. (But if the prompt falls on background, it can segment the wrong thing.)

- **Color replacement inside the masks:**
  - It computes **one mean BGR color per mask** from the *original frame pixels inside that mask*.
  - Then it creates a “flat-color” image where **all pixels in that mask are replaced by that single mean color**.
  - Finally it **alpha-blends** this flat-color mask overlay with the original frame using `--sam-alpha`.
  - So: it **is constant color per segment**, not a local/patchy average.

- **Debug circles:**
  - It draws **two filled circles** at the two prompt points:
    - first prompt: **white** `(255,255,255)`
    - second prompt: **green-ish** `(80,220,80)`
  - These correspond to “mouse0/mouse1” only in the *prompt ordering* sense (and with k-means, that ordering can swap between frames unless you add temporal tracking).

A couple of extra behaviors you might care about:
- **Prompt fallback:** if a frame has too few confident DLC points, it reuses the **last valid prompts** (“last_prompts”) to keep SAM running.
- **Overlaps:** if SAM returns overlapping masks for the two prompts, the code removes the overlap from the smaller mask (simple heuristic).

If you want it to be *exactly* “mouse0 centroid” and “mouse1 centroid” (based on the CSV IDs), run with `--sam-use-dlc-ids`. But given your DLC identity issues, the k-means prompt mode is more likely to land on the two physical mice.

User: Can we use the --mouse0-bgr "25,35,40" --mouse1-bgr "40,35,25" to help sam to select the right segments in case the prompt location is not on the mouse body?

Does sam-alpha need to be 0.0 or 1.0 in order to have a precisely constant color at the segment?

Assistant: ### Using `--mouse0-bgr/--mouse1-bgr` to help SAM
Not with the current implementation — and not directly with SAM in general.

SAM’s `SamPredictor.predict()` takes prompts like **points**, **boxes**, and/or an optional **mask prior**. It does **not** take “expected color” as an input. So those BGR prototypes can’t steer SAM’s segmentation *during* mask generation.

What we *can* do (and it’s a good idea) is use your prototypes **after** SAM produces candidate masks to **select the right mask**:

- For each prompt, ask SAM for multiple masks (`multimask_output=True` already does this).
- For each candidate mask, compute its **mean BGR** (or better: median) and score it by closeness to the expected prototype:
  \[
  \text{score} = \lambda \cdot \text{SAM\_score} - (1-\lambda)\cdot \| \mu_{\text{mask}} - \mu_{\text{prototype}} \|
  \]
- Pick the candidate with best combined score.
- Also add a sanity check: reject masks that are too small/too large.

That would indeed help when the prompt lands on background or on the other mouse.

If you want, I can implement that selection logic next (it’s a clean, contained change in the SAM path).

---

### Does `sam-alpha` need to be 0.0 or 1.0 for constant color?
Yes:

- `--sam-alpha 1.0` → **inside each mask becomes exactly constant** (the mask’s mean color), because you fully replace those pixels with the flat-color overlay.
- `--sam-alpha 0.0` → **no visible effect** (you keep the original frame; masks are computed but don’t change pixels).
- Values in between (e.g. 0.65) → a **blend**: the segment looks “flattened” toward constant color but still retains texture.

So for “precisely constant color in the segment”, use:
```bash
--sam-alpha 1.0
```

- prototypes should be **fixed per mouse** (`--mouse0-bgr/--mouse1-bgr`) or
- inferred per video from a calibration span,

and I’ll patch `overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py` accordingly.

Assistant: from pathlib import Path
import re, os, stat

src_path = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py")
src = src_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")

# 1) Update _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows to use medoids for kmeans mode.
pattern = r"def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows\([\s\S]*?\n\)\s*-> Optional\[np\.ndarray\]:\n([\s\S]*?)\n\n"
# We'll locate function block by name and replace with improved version.
start = src.find("def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows")
if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("Function _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows not found.")
# find end of function by searching next "\ndef " after start
m = re.search(r"\ndef ", src[start+1:])
if not m:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find next def.")
end = start + 1 + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows: pd.DataFrame, min_lik: float, use_dlc_ids: bool) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    \"""
    Return point prompts (2,2) in pixel coords (x,y) for the two mice.

    - If use_dlc_ids: use current 'individual' labels and compute centroids.
    - Else: ignore IDs, kmeans-cluster points into 2 groups in XY, then choose a *medoid* (an actual
      detected point) per cluster to increase the chance that the prompt lies on the mouse body.
    \"""
    rows = rows[rows["likelihood"] >= float(min_lik)]
    if len(rows) < 4:
        return None

    if use_dlc_ids:
        inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) < 2:
            return None
        inds = inds[:2]
        c = []
        for ind in inds:
            sub = rows[rows["individual"].astype(str) == ind]
            if len(sub) < 2:
                return None
            c.append([float(sub["x"].mean()), float(sub["y"].mean())])
        return np.array(c, dtype=np.float32)

    # kmeans in xy
    pts = rows[["x", "y"]].to_numpy(dtype=np.float64)
    try:
        centers, labels = _kmeans2_xy(pts, iters=25)
    except Exception:
        return None

    prompts = []
    for k in (0, 1):
        sub = rows.iloc[np.where(labels == k)[0]]
        if len(sub) == 0:
            return None
        # Prefer an actual detection with high likelihood and close to cluster center.
        cx, cy = float(centers[k, 0]), float(centers[k, 1])
        sub = sub.copy()
        sub["dist2"] = (sub["x"] - cx) ** 2 + (sub["y"] - cy) ** 2
        # score: high likelihood and close
        sub["score"] = sub["likelihood"] * 1.0 - 0.0001 * sub["dist2"]
        best = sub.sort_values(["score", "likelihood"], ascending=False).iloc[0]
        prompts.append([float(best["x"]), float(best["y"])])
    return np.array(prompts, dtype=np.float32)
"""

src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

# 2) Update _sam_segment_two_mice to support prototype-based mask selection + assignment.
start = src.find("def _sam_segment_two_mice")
if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("_sam_segment_two_mice not found")
m = re.search(r"\ndef ", src[start+1:])
end = start + 1 + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _sam_segment_two_mice(
    predictor,
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    prompts_xy: np.ndarray,
    multimask: bool = True,
    proto0_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
    proto1_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray, bool]:
    \"""
    Returns (mask0, mask1, swapped) where mask0 is for mouse0 (proto0) and mask1 for mouse1 (proto1)
    when prototypes are provided. 'swapped' indicates whether prompt order was swapped.

    If prototypes are not provided, returns the best-by-SAM-score mask per prompt, and swapped=False.
    \"""
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    # For each prompt i, get candidate masks and scores
    cand_masks = []
    cand_scores = []
    for i in range(2):
        p = prompts_xy[i].reshape(1, 2)
        labels = np.array([1], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(
            point_coords=p,
            point_labels=labels,
            multimask_output=bool(multimask),
        )
        cand_masks.append(masks.astype(bool))
        cand_scores.append(scores.astype(np.float64))

    # If no prototypes: pick best score per prompt
    if proto0_bgr is None or proto1_bgr is None:
        out = []
        for i in range(2):
            scores = cand_scores[i]
            best = int(np.argmax(scores))
            out.append(cand_masks[i][best])
        return out[0], out[1], False

    proto0 = np.asarray(proto0_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    proto1 = np.asarray(proto1_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    min_area = 300
    max_area = int(0.95 * H * W)

    def best_for_proto(i: int, proto: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, float, float]:
        masks = cand_masks[i]
        scores = cand_scores[i]
        best_mask = masks[int(np.argmax(scores))]
        best_dist = float("inf")
        best_score = float(scores[int(np.argmax(scores))])

        for k in range(masks.shape[0]):
            mk = masks[k]
            area = int(mk.sum())
            if area < min_area or area > max_area:
                continue
            pix = frame_bgr[mk]
            if pix.size == 0:
                continue
            mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float64)  # BGR
            dist = float(np.linalg.norm(mean_col - proto))
            if dist < best_dist - 1e-6:
                best_dist = dist
                best_score = float(scores[k])
                best_mask = mk
            elif abs(dist - best_dist) <= 5.0 and float(scores[k]) > best_score:
                # tie-break by SAM score
                best_score = float(scores[k])
                best_mask = mk

        return best_mask, best_dist, best_score

    # Evaluate both assignments: prompt0->mouse0, prompt1->mouse1  vs swapped
    m00, d00, s00 = best_for_proto(0, proto0)
    m01, d01, s01 = best_for_proto(0, proto1)
    m10, d10, s10 = best_for_proto(1, proto0)
    m11, d11, s11 = best_for_proto(1, proto1)

    cost_noswap = d00 + d11
    cost_swap = d01 + d10

    if cost_swap + 1e-6 < cost_noswap:
        # swap mapping between prompts
        return m10, m01, True  # prompt1->mouse0, prompt0->mouse1
    return m00, m11, False
"""
src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

# 3) Update overlay_video_with_sam to pass prototypes and draw circles as mouse0/mouse1 even if swapped.
# Find signature block and add proto args
# We'll patch by locating function definition and inserting parameters after sam_only.
ov_start = src.find("def overlay_video_with_sam(")
if ov_start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("overlay_video_with_sam not found")
ov_end = src.find(") -> None:", ov_start)
sig = src[ov_start:ov_end+len(") -> None:")]

if "proto0_bgr" not in sig:
    # insert before ) -> None:
    sig_new = sig.replace(
        "    sam_only: bool,\n) -> None:",
        "    sam_only: bool,\n    proto0_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,\n    proto1_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,\n) -> None:"
    )
    src = src.replace(sig, sig_new)

# Now patch call site inside overlay_video_with_sam where _sam_segment_two_mice is called.
src = src.replace(
    "m0, m1 = _sam_segment_two_mice(predictor, out_frame, prompts_xy=prompts, multimask=True)\n"
    "                    out_frame = _overlay_masks_constant_color(out_frame, m0, m1, alpha=float(sam_alpha))\n"
    "                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[0, 0]), int(prompts[0, 1])), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n"
    "                    cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[1, 0]), int(prompts[1, 1])), 4, (80, 220, 80), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n",
    "m0, m1, swapped = _sam_segment_two_mice(\n"
    "                        predictor,\n"
    "                        out_frame,\n"
    "                        prompts_xy=prompts,\n"
    "                        multimask=True,\n"
    "                        proto0_bgr=proto0_bgr,\n"
    "                        proto1_bgr=proto1_bgr,\n"
    "                    )\n"
    "                    out_frame = _overlay_masks_constant_color(out_frame, m0, m1, alpha=float(sam_alpha))\n"
    "                    # draw prompt points: white for mouse0, green for mouse1\n"
    "                    if swapped:\n"
    "                        # prompt1 corresponds to mouse0, prompt0 to mouse1\n"
    "                        cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[1, 0]), int(prompts[1, 1])), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n"
    "                        cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[0, 0]), int(prompts[0, 1])), 4, (80, 220, 80), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n"
    "                    else:\n"
    "                        cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[0, 0]), int(prompts[0, 1])), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n"
    "                        cv2.circle(out_frame, (int(prompts[1, 0]), int(prompts[1, 1])), 4, (80, 220, 80), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)\n"

Assistant: from pathlib import Path
import re, os, stat, numpy as np

src_path = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py")
src = src_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")

# Patch _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows
start = src.find("def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows")
if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("Function _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows not found.")
m = re.search(r"\ndef ", src[start+1:])
if not m:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find next def after _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows.")
end = start + 1 + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows: pd.DataFrame, min_lik: float, use_dlc_ids: bool) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    \"""
    Return point prompts (2,2) in pixel coords (x,y) for the two mice.

    - If use_dlc_ids: use current 'individual' labels and compute centroids.
    - Else: ignore IDs, kmeans-cluster points into 2 groups in XY, then choose a *medoid* (an actual
      detected point) per cluster to increase the chance that the prompt lies on the mouse body.
    \"""
    rows = rows[rows["likelihood"] >= float(min_lik)]
    if len(rows) < 4:
        return None

    if use_dlc_ids:
        inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) < 2:
            return None
        inds = inds[:2]
        c = []
        for ind in inds:
            sub = rows[rows["individual"].astype(str) == ind]
            if len(sub) < 2:
                return None
            c.append([float(sub["x"].mean()), float(sub["y"].mean())])
        return np.array(c, dtype=np.float32)

    pts = rows[["x", "y"]].to_numpy(dtype=np.float64)
    try:
        centers, labels = _kmeans2_xy(pts, iters=25)
    except Exception:
        return None

    prompts = []
    for k in (0, 1):
        idxs = np.where(labels == k)[0]
        if idxs.size == 0:
            return None
        sub = rows.iloc[idxs].copy()
        cx, cy = float(centers[k, 0]), float(centers[k, 1])
        sub["dist2"] = (sub["x"] - cx) ** 2 + (sub["y"] - cy) ** 2
        sub["score"] = sub["likelihood"] * 1.0 - 0.0001 * sub["dist2"]
        best = sub.sort_values(["score", "likelihood"], ascending=False).iloc[0]
        prompts.append([float(best["x"]), float(best["y"])])
    return np.array(prompts, dtype=np.float32)
"""
src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

# Patch _sam_segment_two_mice
start = src.find("def _sam_segment_two_mice")
if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("_sam_segment_two_mice not found")
m = re.search(r"\ndef ", src[start+1:])
if not m:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find next def after _sam_segment_two_mice.")
end = start + 1 + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _sam_segment_two_mice(
    predictor,
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    prompts_xy: np.ndarray,
    multimask: bool = True,
    proto0_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
    proto1_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray, bool]:
    \"""
    Returns (mask0, mask1, swapped).

    - If prototypes are provided (proto0_bgr for mouse0, proto1_bgr for mouse1),
      we select the best SAM mask per prompt by color similarity to the prototype
      (tie-break with SAM score), and also evaluate both prompt-to-mouse assignments
      (no-swap vs swap) to reduce failures when prompt ordering flips.
    - If prototypes are not provided, we just take the best SAM-score mask per prompt.
    \"""
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    cand_masks = []
    cand_scores = []
    for i in range(2):
        p = prompts_xy[i].reshape(1, 2)
        labels = np.array([1], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(
            point_coords=p,
            point_labels=labels,
            multimask_output=bool(multimask),
        )
        cand_masks.append(masks.astype(bool))
        cand_scores.append(scores.astype(np.float64))

    if proto0_bgr is None or proto1_bgr is None:
        out = []
        for i in range(2):
            best = int(np.argmax(cand_scores[i]))
            out.append(cand_masks[i][best])
        return out[0], out[1], False

    proto0 = np.asarray(proto0_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    proto1 = np.asarray(proto1_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    min_area = 300
    max_area = int(0.95 * H * W)

    def best_for_proto(i: int, proto: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, float, float]:
        masks = cand_masks[i]
        scores = cand_scores[i]
        best_idx = int(np.argmax(scores))
        best_mask = masks[best_idx]
        best_dist = float("inf")
        best_score = float(scores[best_idx])

        for k in range(masks.shape[0]):
            mk = masks[k]
            area = int(mk.sum())
            if area < min_area or area > max_area:
                continue
            pix = frame_bgr[mk]
            if pix.size == 0:
                continue
            mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float64)  # BGR
            dist = float(np.linalg.norm(mean_col - proto))
            if dist < best_dist - 1e-6:
                best_dist = dist
                best_score = float(scores[k])
                best_mask = mk
            elif abs(dist - best_dist) <= 5.0 and float(scores[k]) > best_score:
                best_score = float(scores[k])
                best_mask = mk

        if best_dist == float("inf"):
            # fallback: best SAM score
            return masks[best_idx], 1e9, float(scores[best_idx])
        return best_mask, best_dist, best_score

    m00, d00, _ = best_for_proto(0, proto0)
    m01, d01, _ = best_for_proto(0, proto1)
    m10, d10, _ = best_for_proto(1, proto0)
    m11, d11, _ = best_for_proto(1, proto1)

    cost_noswap = d00 + d11
    cost_swap = d01 + d10

    if cost_swap + 1e-6 < cost_noswap:
        return m10, m01, True
    return m00, m11, False
"""
src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

# Patch overlay_video_with_sam signature to accept prototypes
ov_start = src.find("def overlay_video_with_sam(")
if ov_start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("overlay_video_with_sam not found")

        "    sam_only: bool,\n) -> None:",

    )
    src = src.replace(sig, sig_new)

Assistant: Done — I updated the SAM overlay script so that **your fixed prototypes (`--mouse0-bgr/--mouse1-bgr`) are used to choose the “right” SAM mask**, and also to keep the **white/green circles consistently meaning mouse0/mouse1** even when the prompt ordering flips.

[Download overlay_dlc_on_videos_v6.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v6.py)

## What changed vs v5

### 1) Prompts are now more likely to lie on the mouse
When `--sam-use-dlc-ids` is **NOT** set (default), we still do k-means (k=2) in XY, **but** we no longer use the raw centroid (which can fall on background).  
Instead, for each cluster we pick a **medoid prompt**: an *actual detected DLC point* in that cluster (high likelihood + close to cluster center). This substantially reduces “prompt not on body”.

### 2) Prototype-guided mask selection
For each prompt, SAM returns multiple candidate masks (multimask). Previously we picked the one with highest SAM score.

Now, if you provide both:
- `--mouse0-bgr "b,g,r"`
- `--mouse1-bgr "b,g,r"`

…then for each prompt and each candidate mask we compute:
- the **mean BGR of the pixels inside that mask**
- the **L2 distance to the prototype**

We pick the candidate with **smallest color distance** (tie-break: higher SAM score), and we reject obviously bad masks by area (too tiny / too huge).

### 3) Handles prompt ordering flips
Even with k-means, “prompt 0” vs “prompt 1” may swap across frames.  
So we evaluate both assignments:

- (prompt0 → mouse0, prompt1 → mouse1)
- (prompt0 → mouse1, prompt1 → mouse0)

and choose whichever gives **smaller total prototype color distance**.

### 4) Circles match mouse IDs
The **white circle** is always drawn at the prompt that is currently assigned to **mouse0**, and the **green circle** to **mouse1** (even if prompt ordering flips).

## How to run
Example:

```bash
python overlay_dlc_on_videos_v6.py \
  --dlc ../dlc_long.csv \
  --topIn top.mp4 --frontIn front.mp4 --sideIn side.mp4 \
  --topOut top_sam.mp4 --frontOut front_sam.mp4 --sideOut side_sam.mp4 \
  --joinedVideo joined_sam.mp4 \
  --template ../mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
  --sam \
  --sam-checkpoint /path/to/sam_vit_b_01ec64.pth \
  --sam-model-type vit_b \
  --sam-alpha 1.0 \
  --mouse0-bgr "25,35,40" \
  --mouse1-bgr "40,35,25"
```

Notes:
- `--sam-alpha 1.0` makes the segment **exactly constant color** (not blended with original).
- Leave `--sam-use-dlc-ids` **off** unless you’re sure the DLC identities are stable.

If you run this and the segment selection is still wrong when mice overlap heavily, the next upgrade would be to also pass a **box prompt** derived from each cluster’s point cloud (SAM supports boxes), which helps a lot when point prompting alone fails.

Assistant: Yes — your diagnosis is right: the current “hard max area” test (`0.95 * H*W`) is far too weak, so SAM can happily return the **floor** as a “valid” mask. ## What changed in v7

### 1) Hard rejection of huge masks
New CLI option:

- `--sam-max-area-frac` (default **0.35**)  
  Any candidate mask larger than `0.35 * image_area` is rejected.  
This should kill floor-sized segments immediately.

### 2) Expected mouse area learned over frames (EMA) + factor gate
For each view, the code keeps an EMA:

- `ema_area0`, `ema_area1`

On each SAM frame (e.g., every 5th), after selecting masks it updates EMA with the selected mask areas.

When selecting candidate masks, it rejects masks outside:

- `[--sam-area-low * expected_area,  --sam-area-high * expected_area]`
  - defaults: **0.5** and **2.0**

If EMA isn’t available yet, it uses a fallback “expected area” derived from the spread of DLC points (bbox area × 0.6).

This implements your “factor 0.5 / 2.0” rule.

### 3) Prototype distance rejection
New CLI option:

- `--sam-max-color-dist` (default **120**)  
If a mask’s mean BGR is farther than this from the prototype, it’s rejected in the strict pass.

This should also reject the green floor (its mean color is far from your brown/blue prototypes).

### 4) Fixes the broken `print(" ...` line
You’re right: there *was* a broken print (newline inside the string literal) around:
```python
print("
[autoCorrect] Top view...")
```
v7 fixes that.

## How to run (your command, corrected)

Two small notes about your call:

1) You used `--topIn` **twice**. The second one wins, but it’s confusing. Use it once.
2) You were still running **overlay_dlc_on_videos_v5.py**. Use **v7**.

Example:

```bash
python overlay_dlc_on_videos_v7.py \
  --dlc ../dlc_long.csv \
  --topIn ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/cam1_top.mp4 \
  --frontIn ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/cam2_front.mp4 \
  --sideIn ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/cam3_side.mp4 \
  --topOut top_anno.mp4 --frontOut front_anno.mp4 --sideOut side_anno.mp4 \
  --joinedVideo joined_anno.mp4 \
  --template ../mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
  --sam \
  --sam-checkpoint ./sam_vit_b_01ec64.pth \
  --sam-model-type vit_b \
  --sam-alpha 1.0 \
  --mouse0-bgr "25,35,40" --mouse1-bgr "40,35,25" \
  --sam-only --sam-every 5 \
  --sam-max-area-frac 0.25 \
  --sam-area-low 0.5 --sam-area-high 2.0 \
  --sam-max-color-dist 120
```

If the floor still occasionally passes, reduce `--sam-max-area-frac` further (e.g. `0.20`). In top view the mouse should be a relatively small fraction of the frame.

src = src.replace(old_block, new_block)

# 2) Add helper to keep only connected component containing the positive prompt.
if "_keep_component_containing_point" not in src:
    insert_at = src.find("def _sam_load_predictor")
    helper = """
def _keep_component_containing_point(mask: np.ndarray, x: float, y: float) -> np.ndarray:
    \"\"\"Keep only the connected component of `mask` that contains (x,y).\"\"\"
    if mask is None or mask.size == 0:
        return mask
    H, W = mask.shape[:2]
    xi, yi = int(round(x)), int(round(y))
    xi = max(0, min(W - 1, xi))
    yi = max(0, min(H - 1, yi))
    m = mask.astype("uint8")
    num, labels = cv2.connectedComponents(m, connectivity=8)
    if num <= 1:
        return mask
    lab = labels[yi, xi]
    if lab == 0:
        # prompt isn't inside the mask; fall back to largest component
        best_lab = 0
        best_area = -1
        for k in range(1, num):
            area = int((labels == k).sum())
            if area > best_area:
                best_area = area
                best_lab = k
        if best_lab == 0:
            return mask
        return (labels == best_lab)
    return (labels == lab)
"""
    src = src[:insert_at] + helper + "\n" + src[insert_at:]

# 3) Modify SAM segmentation to use negative point at the other mouse centroid, and apply component filtering.
# Find _sam_segment_two_mice definition and replace.

if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("_sam_segment_two_mice not found")
m = re.search(r"\ndef _overlay_masks_constant_color", src[start:])
if not m:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not locate end of _sam_segment_two_mice")
end = start + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _sam_segment_two_mice(
    predictor,
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    prompts_xy: np.ndarray,
    multimask: bool = True,
    proto0_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
    proto1_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray, bool]:
    \"""
    Returns (mask0, mask1, swapped).

    Improvements vs v6/v7:
    - Prompts are body-center-ish (centroids).
    - Each segmentation uses TWO point prompts:
        positive at its centroid, negative at the other mouse centroid.
      This reduces cases where the mask bleeds into background/floor or captures both mice.
    - If a chosen mask contains disconnected components, we keep only the component
      containing the positive prompt point (fixes 'extra disconnected segment' artifacts).

    Prototype guidance is still used (if provided) to choose among SAM multimasks
    and to decide whether prompts should be swapped.
    \"""
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    p0 = prompts_xy[0].astype(np.float32)
    p1 = prompts_xy[1].astype(np.float32)

    cand_masks = []
    cand_scores = []
    pos_points = []

    for i in range(2):
        pos = p0 if i == 0 else p1
        neg = p1 if i == 0 else p0
        point_coords = np.stack([pos, neg], axis=0).astype(np.float32)
        point_labels = np.array([1, 0], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(
            point_coords=point_coords,
            point_labels=point_labels,
            multimask_output=bool(multimask),
        )
        cand_masks.append(masks.astype(bool))
        cand_scores.append(scores.astype(np.float64))
        pos_points.append(pos)

    if proto0_bgr is None or proto1_bgr is None:
        out = []
        for i in range(2):
            best = int(np.argmax(cand_scores[i]))
            mk = cand_masks[i][best]
            # keep component containing positive prompt
            mk = _keep_component_containing_point(mk, float(pos_points[i][0]), float(pos_points[i][1]))
            out.append(mk)
        return out[0], out[1], False

    proto0 = np.asarray(proto0_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    proto1 = np.asarray(proto1_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    min_area = 300
    max_area = int(0.35 * H * W)  # stronger default than earlier versions

    def best_for_proto(i: int, proto: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, float]:
        masks = cand_masks[i]
        scores = cand_scores[i]
        pos = pos_points[i]
        best_mask = None
        best_dist = float("inf")
        best_sam = -1.0

        for k in range(masks.shape[0]):
            mk = masks[k]
            mk = _keep_component_containing_point(mk, float(pos[0]), float(pos[1]))
            area = int(mk.sum())
            if area < min_area or area > max_area:
                continue
            pix = frame_bgr[mk]
            if pix.size == 0:
                continue
            mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float64)
            dist = float(np.linalg.norm(mean_col - proto))
            sam_sc = float(scores[k])
            if dist < best_dist - 1e-6 or (abs(dist - best_dist) <= 5.0 and sam_sc > best_sam):
                best_dist = dist
                best_sam = sam_sc
                best_mask = mk

        if best_mask is None:
            # fallback: best SAM score, still component-filtered
            best = int(np.argmax(scores))
            mk = masks[best]
            mk = _keep_component_containing_point(mk, float(pos[0]), float(pos[1]))
            return mk, 1e9
        return best_mask, best_dist

    m00, d00 = best_for_proto(0, proto0)
    m01, d01 = best_for_proto(0, proto1)
    m10, d10 = best_for_proto(1, proto0)
    m11, d11 = best_for_proto(1, proto1)

    cost_noswap = d00 + d11
    cost_swap = d01 + d10

    if cost_swap + 1e-6 < cost_noswap:
        return m10, m01, True
    return m00, m11, False
"""
src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

# 4) Ensure overlay_video_with_sam draws circles at the centroids even when sam_every>1 (draw every frame if prompts exist).
# We'll patch inside overlay_video_with_sam loop: after prompts computed (even if not do sam) draw circles.
# Find the line: "if sam_every <= 1 or (frame_idx % sam_every == 0):"
anchor = "        if sam_every <= 1 or (frame_idx % sam_every == 0):\n"
idx = src.find(anchor)
if idx == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find sam_every conditional")

# We'll add drawing of prompt points immediately after prompts are set/updated and before try/except.
# Locate within block: after last_prompts updated.
needle = "            if prompts is not None:\n"
idx2 = src.find(needle, idx)
if idx2 == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find 'if prompts is not None' inside SAM block")

# Insert a line that draws circles even if segmentation fails; but we already draw later. Keep as-is.

# Write v8
out_path = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v8.py")

import re, os, stat

src_path = Path("/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v7.py")
src = src_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")

# 1) Replace _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows block until _sam_load_predictor

new_block = """def _two_mouse_prompts_from_rows(rows: pd.DataFrame, min_lik: float, use_dlc_ids: bool) -> Optional[np.ndarray]:
    \"""
    Return point prompts (2,2) in pixel coords (x,y) for the two mice.

    v5 worked well because prompts were near the *mouse body center*.
    In v6/v7, using a detected keypoint as prompt often placed it on the body margins
    (nose/paws/tail), and sometimes off-body. So in kmeans mode we intentionally use
    the kmeans centroids (not medoids).

    - If use_dlc_ids: use current 'individual' labels and compute centroids.
    - Else: ignore IDs and return the 2 kmeans centroids in XY.
    \"""
    rows = rows[rows["likelihood"] >= float(min_lik)]
    if len(rows) < 4:
        return None

    if use_dlc_ids:
        inds = sorted(rows["individual"].dropna().astype(str).unique().tolist())
        if len(inds) < 2:
            return None
        inds = inds[:2]
        c = []
        for ind in inds:
            sub = rows[rows["individual"].astype(str) == ind]
            if len(sub) < 2:
                return None
            c.append([float(sub["x"].mean()), float(sub["y"].mean())])
        return np.array(c, dtype=np.float32)

    pts = rows[["x", "y"]].to_numpy(dtype=np.float64)
    try:
        centers, _ = _kmeans2_xy(pts, iters=25)
    except Exception:
        return None
    return centers.astype(np.float32)
"""
src = src.replace(old_block, new_block)

# 2) Insert connected-component helper before _sam_load_predictor if not present
if "def _keep_component_containing_point" not in src:
    insert_at = src.find("def _sam_load_predictor")
    if insert_at == -1:
        raise RuntimeError("_sam_load_predictor not found for insertion")
    helper = """
def _keep_component_containing_point(mask: np.ndarray, x: float, y: float) -> np.ndarray:
    \"\"\"Keep only the connected component of `mask` that contains (x,y).\"\"\"
    if mask is None or mask.size == 0:
        return mask
    H, W = mask.shape[:2]
    xi, yi = int(round(x)), int(round(y))
    xi = max(0, min(W - 1, xi))
    yi = max(0, min(H - 1, yi))
    m = mask.astype(np.uint8)
    num, labels = cv2.connectedComponents(m, connectivity=8)
    if num <= 1:
        return mask
    lab = labels[yi, xi]
    if lab == 0:
        # Prompt isn't inside the mask; keep the largest component.
        best_lab = 0
        best_area = -1
        for k in range(1, num):
            area = int((labels == k).sum())
            if area > best_area:
                best_area = area
                best_lab = k
        if best_lab == 0:
            return mask
        return (labels == best_lab)
    return (labels == lab)
"""
    src = src[:insert_at] + helper + "\n" + src[insert_at:]

# 3) Replace _sam_segment_two_mice up to _overlay_masks_constant_color
start = src.find("def _sam_segment_two_mice")
if start == -1:
    raise RuntimeError("_sam_segment_two_mice not found")
m = re.search(r"\ndef _overlay_masks_constant_color", src[start:])
if not m:
    raise RuntimeError("Could not find _overlay_masks_constant_color after _sam_segment_two_mice")
end = start + m.start()
old_func = src[start:end]

new_func = """def _sam_segment_two_mice(
    predictor,
    frame_bgr: np.ndarray,
    prompts_xy: np.ndarray,
    multimask: bool = True,
    proto0_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
    proto1_bgr: Optional[np.ndarray] = None,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray, bool]:
    \"""
    Returns (mask0, mask1, swapped).

    Changes to address v6/v7 regressions:
      1) Each mouse segmentation uses TWO prompts:
         - positive point at its centroid
         - negative point at the other mouse centroid
         This discourages selecting large background/floor segments and reduces "both mice" masks.
      2) If a selected mask contains disconnected components, keep only the component containing
         the positive prompt (prevents extra disconnected background blobs).
      3) Prototypes (if provided) are used to choose among SAM multimasks and to decide swap.

    Note: Strong global area caps and EMA area gating are handled outside this function (v7 logic),
    but we also include a stricter default max_area here as a last-resort safeguard.
    \"""
    img_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    predictor.set_image(img_rgb)

    p0 = prompts_xy[0].astype(np.float32)
    p1 = prompts_xy[1].astype(np.float32)

    cand_masks = []
    cand_scores = []
    pos_points = []

    for i in range(2):
        pos = p0 if i == 0 else p1
        neg = p1 if i == 0 else p0
        point_coords = np.stack([pos, neg], axis=0).astype(np.float32)
        point_labels = np.array([1, 0], dtype=np.int32)
        masks, scores, _ = predictor.predict(
            point_coords=point_coords,
            point_labels=point_labels,
            multimask_output=bool(multimask),
        )
        cand_masks.append(masks.astype(bool))
        cand_scores.append(scores.astype(np.float64))
        pos_points.append(pos)

    def comp_filter(i: int, mk: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
        pos = pos_points[i]
        return _keep_component_containing_point(mk, float(pos[0]), float(pos[1]))

    if proto0_bgr is None or proto1_bgr is None:
        out = []
        for i in range(2):
            best = int(np.argmax(cand_scores[i]))
            mk = comp_filter(i, cand_masks[i][best])
            out.append(mk)
        return out[0], out[1], False

    proto0 = np.asarray(proto0_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    proto1 = np.asarray(proto1_bgr, dtype=np.float64).reshape(3)
    H, W = frame_bgr.shape[:2]
    min_area = 300
    max_area = int(0.35 * H * W)

    def best_for_proto(i: int, proto: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, float]:
        masks = cand_masks[i]
        scores = cand_scores[i]
        best_mask = None
        best_dist = float("inf")
        best_sam = -1.0

        for k in range(masks.shape[0]):
            mk = comp_filter(i, masks[k])
            area = int(mk.sum())
            if area < min_area or area > max_area:
                continue
            pix = frame_bgr[mk]
            if pix.size == 0:
                continue
            mean_col = pix.reshape(-1, 3).mean(axis=0).astype(np.float64)
            dist = float(np.linalg.norm(mean_col - proto))
            sam_sc = float(scores[k])
            if dist < best_dist - 1e-6 or (abs(dist - best_dist) <= 5.0 and sam_sc > best_sam):
                best_dist = dist
                best_sam = sam_sc
                best_mask = mk

        if best_mask is None:
            # fallback: best SAM score (still component filtered)
            best = int(np.argmax(scores))
            mk = comp_filter(i, masks[best])
            return mk, 1e9

        return best_mask, best_dist

    m00, d00 = best_for_proto(0, proto0)
    m01, d01 = best_for_proto(0, proto1)
    m10, d10 = best_for_proto(1, proto0)
    m11, d11 = best_for_proto(1, proto1)

    cost_noswap = d00 + d11
    cost_swap = d01 + d10

    if cost_swap + 1e-6 < cost_noswap:
        return m10, m01, True
    return m00, m11, False
"""
src = src.replace(old_func, new_func)

Assistant: You’re reading the symptoms correctly:

- **v6** got worse because I changed the prompt from a *center-ish* point to a **detected keypoint** (“medoid”). DLC keypoints are often on the **boundary** of the body (nose, paws, tail), so the dot moves to the margin.
- **v7** got worse again because it inherited that medoid-style prompting, and once the dot is off-body, SAM can easily snap to “big, easy” regions (like the green floor).
- The “two disconnected colored segments” is a classic SAM failure mode when the chosen mask contains multiple components. The fix is to **keep only the connected component containing the prompt point**.

### Fix: v8
I created a new version that restores what made **v5** good, and adds two robustifiers:

1) **Prompts are again the k-means centroids** (body-center-ish), not medoids.  
2) Each SAM call uses **two point prompts**:
   - **positive** at its centroid  
   - **negative** at the *other* mouse centroid  
   This discourages merging mice and reduces floor/bleed.
3) After a mask is chosen, it keeps **only the connected component containing the positive prompt** (kills disconnected background blobs).

[Download overlay_dlc_on_videos_v8.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_on_videos_v8.py)

---

## Why this should bring you back to v5 behavior (but more stable)
- v5’s dot was “in the middle” because it was a cluster centroid. v8 restores that.
- The negative point prompt helps when mice are close or when the centroid is near a boundary.
- Component filtering prevents the “mouse + random blob somewhere else” artifact.

---

## About the “carriage return behind print”
You’re right that there was a broken `print("...` line in some intermediate versions. v8 is generated from v7 (where that was already fixed), so that particular syntax problem should be gone.

If you still see any strange prompt placement with v8, the next step would be to add a **box prompt** (DLC-cluster bounding box) in addition to the points — that’s the most reliable way to prevent floor selection when prompts are imperfect.
